Proof of Prophetic Infallibility and Response to Objections
Author proves prophetic infallibility by necessary consequences and answers objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof for prophetic infallibility based on necessary consequences, and how apparent scriptural evidence of prophetic sins is interpreted.

Core Idea
If prophets could sin, they could not be followed — that is the central proof for their infallibility.

This passage presents the key rational argument for prophetic infallibility: a reductio ad absurdum showing that any sin by a prophet would have unacceptable consequences. It also addresses the apparent contradiction from scriptural reports of prophets sinning, offering a hermeneutical framework to reconcile them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the flow from the proof to the objection and the answer.
The author uses a compressed style; the proof is a series of conditional consequences.
2
Identify the consequences of sin
List the six consequences mentioned if prophets were to sin. Understand why each consequence is unacceptable.
These include prohibition of following, rejection of testimony, etc.
3
Analyze the response to objections
Note the opponent's objection based on prophetic repentance and the author's response: rejecting weak reports and interpreting strong ones.
The response uses principles of hadith criticism and theological interpretation.
4
Reflect on the methodology
Consider how the author uses necessary consequences (luzum) to prove a theological point, and how he handles apparent textual conflicts.
This is a classic kalam method: combining rational necessity with textual interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لنا لو صدر عنهم الذنب، لزم حرمة اتباعهم، ورد شهادتهم، ووجوب زجرهم، واستحقاقهم العذاب والذم، وعدم نيلهم عهد النبوة وكونهم غير مخلصين وغير مسارعين في الخيرات وغير معدودين من المصطفين الأخيار، واللوازم منتفية، وفي قيام بعض الوجوم على الصغيرة، وسهو الكبيرة نظر. احتج المخالف بما نقل من نسبة المعصية والذنب إليهم، ومن توبتهم واستغفارهم. والجواب إجمالاً رد ما نقل أحاداً وحمل المتواتر والمنصوص على السهو، أو ترك الأولى، أو ما قبل البعثة، أو نحو ذلك والتفاصيل في التفاسير
For us: if sin were to occur from them, then it would necessitate the prohibition of following them, the rejection of their testimony, the necessity of rebuking them, their deserving punishment and blame, their not attaining the covenant of prophethood, their being not sincere, not hastening in good deeds, and not being counted among the chosen righteous. These consequences are negated. Regarding the occurrence of some objectionable acts concerning minor sins or forgetfulness of major sins, there is consideration. The opponent objects by what has been reported of attributing disobedience and sin to them, and of their repentance and seeking forgiveness. The answer, in summary, is to reject what is reported as isolated reports, and to interpret the mutawatir and nusus (clear texts) as referring to forgetfulness, or leaving the better (tark al-awla), or before the prophethood, or something similar. The details are in the exegeses.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage contains the main proof for prophetic infallibility and the response to an objection. The proof is an argument from necessary consequences: if prophets were to commit sins, then it would become obligatory to avoid following them, to reject their testimony, to rebuke them, and they would deserve punishment, blame, and would not be worthy of prophethood. Since all these consequences are false (the prophets are indeed followed, their testimony accepted, etc.), the premise that they sin must be false. The author then notes that there is some consideration (nazar) regarding the occurrence of minor faults or forgetfulness of major sins. He then addresses an objection: the opponent cites reports where prophets are said to have sinned, repented, and sought forgiveness. The response is to reject the reliability of such reports (especially isolated ones) and to interpret the well-established reports as referring to forgetfulness, leaving the better (tark al-awla), or actions before prophethood. The author concludes by referring to the detailed treatment in exegeses. Note the logical structure: a reductio ad absurdum (luzum) followed by a hermeneutical defense of the texts that seem to indicate sin.

ما قبل البعثة
متواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verses where prophets repent and seek forgiveness prove that they committed major sins.
Correction: These reports are either isolated (ahad) and thus rejected, or well-established and interpreted as forgetfulness, leaving the better, or actions before prophethood.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Prophetic infallibility is established by the necessary consequences of sin, and scriptural evidence to the contrary is interpreted according to established principles.

Categorizing Sins Relative to the Prophetic Miracle
Categorization of sins relative to the prophetic miracle and statement of the majority view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise categorization of sins that could be attributed to prophets and why the crucial category is sins that contradict the miracle (such as lying in conveying).

Core Idea
The miracle only guarantees truthfulness in conveying revelation; other sins must be categorized.

This lesson builds on the principle that miracles establish prophetic truthfulness. The author then presents a complete taxonomy of any sin imagined to issue from a prophet, classifying it first by its relation to the miracle, then by its type, gravity, intentionality, and timing. Understanding this categorization is essential to grasp the scope of prophetic infallibility ('isma).

Guided Path
1
Recall the function of the miracle
Before diving into the classification, remember that the miracle (mu'jiza) confirms the prophet's truthfulness in his claim and his conveying of revelation. This is the starting point.
Note that the passage begins with 'it has preceded that...' referring to earlier discussion.
2
Trace the first division: contradictory to the miracle or not
The first split is between sins that directly contradict the miracle's implication (like lying about revelation) and those that do not. Identify this crucial branch.
The example given is lying regarding tabligh (conveying).
3
Follow the subdivisions of non-contradictory sins
Those sins are further divided into kufr versus other sins, then major/minor repulsive/non-repulsive, then deliberate/forgetful, before/after prophethood. See how the classification covers all possibilities.
Notice the precision: minor sins are split into 'repulsive' and 'non-repulsive'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في عصمة الأنبياء، وقد سبق أن المعجزة تقتضي الصدق في دعوى النبوة وما يتعلق بها من التبليغ ، وشرعية الأحكام . فما يتوهم صدوره عن الأنبياء من القبائح إما أن يكون منافياً لما يقتضيه المعجزة كالكذب فيما يتعلق بالتبليغ أو لا . والثاني إما أن يكون كفراً ومعصية غيره، وهي إما أن تكون كبيرة كالقتل والزنا ، أو صغيرة منفرة كسرقة لقمة ، والتطفيف بحبة . أوغير منفرة ككذبة ، وهم بمعصية . كل ذلك إما عمداً أو سهواً . وبعد البعثة أو قبلها . والجمهور على وجوب عصمتهم (۱) عما ينافي مقتضى المعجزة، وقد جوزه القاضي سهواً زعماً منه أنه لا يدخل في التصديق المقصود بالمعجزة وعن الكفر ، وقد جوزه الأزارقة من الخوارج بناء على تجويزهم الذنب مع قولهم بأن كل ذنب كفر، وجوز الشيعة إظهاره تقية واحترازاً عن إلقاء النفس في التهلكة ورد بأن أولى الأوقات بالتقية ابتداع الدعوة لضعف الداعي ، وشوكة المخالف وكذا عن تعمد الكبائر بعد البعثة، فعندنا سمعاً، وعند المعتزلة عقلاً، وجوزه الحشوية إما لعدم دليل الامتناع ، وإما لما سيجيء من شبه الوقوع
Concerning the infallibility of the prophets: it has preceded that the miracle necessitates truthfulness in the claim of prophethood and what pertains to it of conveying and the legality of rulings. So whatever evil deeds are imagined to occur from the prophets: either (1) it contradicts what the miracle necessitates, like lying concerning conveying, or (2) it does not. The second kind is either kufr or another disobedience. That disobedience is either a major sin (kabira) like murder and adultery, or a minor sin (saghira) that is repulsive (munaffira) like stealing a morsel or cheating by a grain, or non-repulsive like a lie or an intention of disobedience. All of this is either deliberate or by forgetfulness, and either after the prophethood or before it. The majority (jumhur) hold that it is obligatory for them to be immune from what contradicts the requirement of the miracle. Al-Qadi permitted it (sin) out of forgetfulness, claiming that it does not affect the attestation intended by the miracle. Regarding kufr, the Azariqa from the Kharijites permitted it, based on their permitting sin while holding that every sin is kufr. The Shi'a permitted its manifestation dissimulation (taqiyya) to avoid self-destruction, but it is replied that the most appropriate time for dissimulation is the beginning of the call due to the weakness of the caller and the strength of the opponent. Likewise, regarding deliberate major sins after prophethood – according to us (Ash'aris) it is by revelation, according to the Mu'tazila by reason; the Hashwiyya permitted it, either due to lack of proof of impossibility or due to what will come of the semblance of occurrence.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage provides a systematic categorization of all possible sins that could be attributed to prophets, serving as a comprehensive restatement of the issue. The author begins by recalling that miracles demand truthfulness in the prophetic claim. He then divides imagined evil deeds: those that contradict the miracle (e.g., lying in conveying) and those that do not. The latter are further divided into kufr and other sins, which are then classified as major, minor repulsive, and minor non-repulsive. Additional dimensions include deliberateness vs. forgetfulness, and before or after prophethood. The majority view is that immunity (isma) is required only from what contradicts the miracle. The author then reviews the positions of various groups: al-Qadi permits forgetfulness; the Azariqa permit kufr; the Shi'a permit taqiyya but that is rejected; for deliberate major sins, Ash'aris say revelation forbids, Mu'tazila say reason forbids, and Hashwiyya permit due to lack of proof or because of apparent evidence. This passage is a summary of the earlier detailed discussion, and it highlights the consensus on the core of 'isma while noting divergent views on peripheral aspects.

Key Terms
عصمة
المعجزة
قبائح
كفر
كبيرة
صغيرة منفرة
صغيرة غير منفرة
عمد
سهو
بعد البعثة
قبل البعثة
الجمهور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophetic infallibility means prophets are entirely sinless and cannot commit any sin whatsoever.
Correction: The passage clarifies that immunity is limited to sins that contradict the requirement of the miracle (especially lying in conveying revelation); other types of sins (major, minor, etc.) are not necessarily excluded by the miracle, though the majority position is that they are immune from them by additional revelation or reason.

Checkpoint

A) Minor sin (saghira)
B) Lying concerning conveying (al-kadhib fi ma yata'allaq bi al-tabligh)
C) Major sin (kabira)
D) Sin committed before prophethood

Key Takeaway
The miracle of prophethood only guarantees truthfulness in conveying revelation; other sins are categorized but the majority view is that prophets are immune only from those that undermine this core function.

Sectarian Positions on the Limits of Prophetic Infallibility
Enumeration of sectarian positions on prophetic infallibility regarding forgetfulness, kufr, taqiyya, and deliberate major sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of various Islamic sects regarding which sins prophets may commit, especially in relation to kufr, forgetfulness, dissimulation, and deliberate major sins.

Core Idea
Different sects stretched or limited prophetic immunity based on their theological principles about sin and faith.

After establishing the basic categorization of sins, the author turns to the diverse views of Islamic sects and scholars. Each group's stance on prophetic immunity reflects its broader theological commitments—whether it permits sins of forgetfulness, kufr, dissimulation (taqiyya), or deliberate major sins. This lesson unpacks those positions and their justifications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the groups mentioned
The passage lists al-Qadi (Abd al-Jabbar?), al-Azariqa (Kharijites), al-Shi'a, and al-Hashwiyya. Also implicitly the Ash'ari and Mu'tazila positions. Note each one's stance.
Al-Qadi is likely Qadi Abd al-Jabbar, a Mu'tazilite.
2
Understand al-Qadi's view on forgetfulness
Al-Qadi permitted sins of forgetfulness, claiming that forgetfulness does not affect the attestation intended by the miracle.
This is a nuanced exception.
3
Analyze the Azariqa position on kufr
The Azariqa (a Kharijite subsect) permitted kufr from prophets because they considered every sin as kufr.
Their reasoning is based on equating all sins with disbelief.
4
Review the Shi'a view on taqiyya
The Shi'a permitted prophets to manifest kufr under dissimulation (taqiyya) to avoid self-destruction, but this is rebutted by reasoning that taqiyya is more appropriate at the beginning of the prophetic call.
The rebuttal is part of the passage.
5
Compare positions on deliberate major sins after prophethood
On deliberate major sins after prophethood: Ash'aris hold it is forbidden by revelation (sam'an), Mu'tazila by reason ('aqlan), and Hashwiyya permitted it due to lack of proof or apparent conflicting evidence.
The Hashwiyya are a group that accepted traditions literally without critical thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في عصمة الأنبياء، وقد سبق أن المعجزة تقتضي الصدق في دعوى النبوة وما يتعلق بها من التبليغ ، وشرعية الأحكام . فما يتوهم صدوره عن الأنبياء من القبائح إما أن يكون منافياً لما يقتضيه المعجزة كالكذب فيما يتعلق بالتبليغ أو لا . والثاني إما أن يكون كفراً ومعصية غيره، وهي إما أن تكون كبيرة كالقتل والزنا ، أو صغيرة منفرة كسرقة لقمة ، والتطفيف بحبة . أوغير منفرة ككذبة ، وهم بمعصية . كل ذلك إما عمداً أو سهواً . وبعد البعثة أو قبلها . والجمهور على وجوب عصمتهم (۱) عما ينافي مقتضى المعجزة، وقد جوزه القاضي سهواً زعماً منه أنه لا يدخل في التصديق المقصود بالمعجزة وعن الكفر ، وقد جوزه الأزارقة من الخوارج بناء على تجويزهم الذنب مع قولهم بأن كل ذنب كفر، وجوز الشيعة إظهاره تقية واحترازاً عن إلقاء النفس في التهلكة ورد بأن أولى الأوقات بالتقية ابتداع الدعوة لضعف الداعي ، وشوكة المخالف وكذا عن تعمد الكبائر بعد البعثة، فعندنا سمعاً، وعند المعتزلة عقلاً، وجوزه الحشوية إما لعدم دليل الامتناع ، وإما لما سيجيء من شبه الوقوع
Concerning the infallibility of the prophets: it has preceded that the miracle necessitates truthfulness in the claim of prophethood and what pertains to it of conveying and the legality of rulings. So whatever evil deeds are imagined to occur from the prophets: either (1) it contradicts what the miracle necessitates, like lying concerning conveying, or (2) it does not. The second kind is either kufr or another disobedience. That disobedience is either a major sin (kabira) like murder and adultery, or a minor sin (saghira) that is repulsive (munaffira) like stealing a morsel or cheating by a grain, or non-repulsive like a lie or an intention of disobedience. All of this is either deliberate or by forgetfulness, and either after the prophethood or before it. The majority (jumhur) hold that it is obligatory for them to be immune from what contradicts the requirement of the miracle. Al-Qadi permitted it (sin) out of forgetfulness, claiming that it does not affect the attestation intended by the miracle. Regarding kufr, the Azariqa from the Kharijites permitted it, based on their permitting sin while holding that every sin is kufr. The Shi'a permitted its manifestation dissimulation (taqiyya) to avoid self-destruction, but it is replied that the most appropriate time for dissimulation is the beginning of the call due to the weakness of the caller and the strength of the opponent. Likewise, regarding deliberate major sins after prophethood – according to us (Ash'aris) it is by revelation, according to the Mu'tazila by reason; the Hashwiyya permitted it, either due to lack of proof of impossibility or due to what will come of the semblance of occurrence.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage provides a systematic categorization of all possible sins that could be attributed to prophets, serving as a comprehensive restatement of the issue. The author begins by recalling that miracles demand truthfulness in the prophetic claim. He then divides imagined evil deeds: those that contradict the miracle (e.g., lying in conveying) and those that do not. The latter are further divided into kufr and other sins, which are then classified as major, minor repulsive, and minor non-repulsive. Additional dimensions include deliberateness vs. forgetfulness, and before or after prophethood. The majority view is that immunity (isma) is required only from what contradicts the miracle. The author then reviews the positions of various groups: al-Qadi permits forgetfulness; the Azariqa permit kufr; the Shi'a permit taqiyya but that is rejected; for deliberate major sins, Ash'aris say revelation forbids, Mu'tazila say reason forbids, and Hashwiyya permit due to lack of proof or because of apparent evidence. This passage is a summary of the earlier detailed discussion, and it highlights the consensus on the core of 'isma while noting divergent views on peripheral aspects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that all Islamic sects agree on the exact boundaries of prophetic infallibility.
Correction: As this passage shows, there is significant disagreement, with some groups permitting even kufr or deliberate major sins, while others restrict immunity to only what contradicts the miracle.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group permitted prophets to commit kufr?
A) Al-Qadi
B) The Azariqa
C) The Shi'a
D) The Hashwiyya

Key Takeaway
Sectarian views on prophetic immunity range from very restrictive (only sins contradicting miracle forbidden) to very permissive (allowing even kufr), reflecting each sect's deeper theological principles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Kharijites equated every sin with kufr, leading them to permit prophets to commit kufr. When you sin, do you tend to see it as a complete rejection of faith? How does that affect your hope in Allah's mercy? What step will you take today to break this cycle of despair or excuse-making?
?
The Shi'a permitted outward kufr under taqiyya to avoid self-destruction. Reflect on a time you hid or compromised your faith to avoid difficulty. Was it truly necessary, or did fear drive you? What does this passage teach you about trusting Allah's protection even when it is costly?
?
Al-Qadi claimed that forgetful sin does not affect prophethood. How often do you excuse your own moral failings as mere forgetfulness, ignoring their impact on your witness as a Muslim? Commit to one area where you will intentionally guard against spiritual negligence starting this week.

Objection and Answer on Prophetic Sins
Al-Taftazani presents the objection and his summarized answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani defends the doctrine of prophetic infallibility against apparent Quranic attributions of sin.

Core Idea
Prophetic 'errors' are forgetfulness or leaving the better, not actual sins.

This passage presents a classic theological objection and its concise answer. Opponents of prophetic infallibility cite verses where prophets repent or are said to sin. Al-Taftazani outlines the Sunni method of dealing with such texts: weak reports are rejected, while strong ones are reinterpreted.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The first sentence states the opponent's argument: transmitted reports attribute sin and repentance to prophets. Note the types of evidence they use.
Opponents rely on both explicit Quranic verses and hadith.
2
Read the answer
The second sentence gives the summary answer. It has two parts: reject weak (ahaad) reports and interpret strong (mutawatir) reports allegorically.
Take note of the categories: forgetfulness (sahu), leaving the better (tark al-awla), and pre-prophetic events.
3
Reflect on the logic
Consider why these categories preserve infallibility. Forgetting a human action is not a sin; leaving the better is not a transgression; pre-prophetic events do not affect prophethood.
This interpretive principle is key to understanding Sunni 'isma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احتج المخالف بما نقل من نسبة المعصية والذنب إليهم، ومن توبتهم واستغفارهم. والجواب إجمالاً رد ما نقل أحاداً وحمل المتواتر والمنصوص على السهو، أو ترك الأولى، أو ما قبل البعثة، أو نحو ذلك والتفاصيل في التفاسير.
The opponent argued by what is transmitted of attributing disobedience and sin to them (the prophets), and of their repentance and seeking forgiveness. The answer in summary is to reject what was transmitted as isolated (ahaad) reports, and to interpret the mutawatir and explicit texts as referring to forgetfulness, or abandoning the better (tark al-awla), or what occurred before the prophethood, or similar [interpretations]. And the details are in the commentaries.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objector cites Qur'anic verses that seem to attribute sins to prophets (e.g., verses about repentance). The answer explains that such reports are either weak (ahaad) or, if authentic (mutawatir), are interpreted figuratively: as forgetfulness, abandoning the better, or events before prophethood. The full details are left to exegesis.

Key Terms
معصية
ذنب
توبة
استغفار
سهو
ترك الأولى
أحاد
متواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Belief that prophets committed sins because the Quran mentions their repentance.
Correction: Such verses are interpreted metaphorically or refer to pre-prophetic actions, preserving their infallibility.

Checkpoint
How does al-Taftazani answer the objection that prophets repented for sins?
A) He denies the verses are authentic.
B) He interprets them as referring to forgetfulness, abandoning the better, or pre-prophetic events.
C) He claims prophets only sinned unintentionally.
D) He says the verses are abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani defends prophetic infallibility by classifying problematic reports as weak or interpretable as forgetfulness, leaving the better, or pre-prophetic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses mentioning prophets' repentance, do you instinctively think they sinned? How can Al-Taftazani's approach train you to question your first impression and seek deeper interpretations?
?
Have you ever dismissed a hadith because it seemed to contradict a core belief? How does Al-Taftazani's method of weighing reports and reinterpreting texts challenge you to handle difficult evidence with more care and humility?
?
If you believe prophets are sinless, how does this lesson affect your understanding of their humanity? Are you willing to accept that their 'errors' were only forgetfulness or leaving the better, even when the text uses strong words like 'sin' and 'repentance'? What change in your reading habits does this demand?

Classification of Sins in Relation to Prophethood
Al-Taftazani enumerates categories of sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the categories of sins that prophets might be fancied to commit, based on their relation to the miracle.

Core Idea
Sins are classified by their relation to the miracle, kind, repulsiveness, and timing.

Before diving into the positions on prophetic infallibility, al-Taftazani establishes a precise classification of what is meant by 'sin' in this context. He distinguishes sins that contradict the miracle (like lying) from those that do not, and further breaks down the latter into disbelief, major sins, and minor sins, with a further division into repulsive and non-repulsive. He also notes the dimensions of intention and timing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the logical flow: starting from the prerequisite miracle, then the main division, then subdivisions.
2
Identify the primary division
Find the first major division: sins that contradict the miracle (like lying) vs. those that do not. Underline this in your mind.
This is the most important distinction because it directly impacts infallibility.
3
Break down the second category
The second category is further divided into disbelief and other sins. Then other sins are divided into major and minor. Minor sins are further split into repulsive and non-repulsive.
Make a mental tree: sin → contradictory or not → not contradictory → disbelief or other → other → major or minor → minor → repulsive or non-repulsive.
4
Note the additional dimensions
The passage also mentions that all these sins can be intentional or inadvertent, and can occur before or after prophethood. These dimensions affect the rulings that follow.
These dimensions will be crucial for understanding the different positions in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في عصمة الأنبياء، وقد سبق أن المعجزة تقتضي الصدق في دعوى النبوة وما يتعلق بها من التبليغ، وشرعية الأحكام. فما يتوهم صدوره عن الأنبياء من القبائح إما أن يكون منافياً لما يقتضيه المعجزة كالكذب فيما يتعلق بالتبليغ أو لا. والثاني إما أن يكون كفراً ومعصية غيره، وهي إما أن تكون كبيرة كالقتل والزنا، أو صغيرة منفرة كسرقة لقمة، والتطفيف بحبة. أو غير منفرة ككذبة، وهم بمعصية. كل ذلك إما عمداً أو سهواً، وبعد البعثة أو قبلها. والجمهور على وجوب عصمتهم عما ينافي مقتضى المعجزة، وقد جوزه القاضي سهواً زعماً منه أنه لا يدخل في التصديق المقصود بالمعجزة وعن الكفر، وقد جوزه الأزارقة من الخوارج بناء على تجويزهم الذنب مع قولهم بأن كل ذنب كفر، وجوز الشيعة إظهاره تقية واحترازاً عن إلقاء النفس في التهلكة ورد بأن أولى الأوقات بالتقية ابتداع الدعوة لضعف الداعي، وشوكة المخالف وكذا عن تعمد الكبائر بعد البعثة، فعندنا سمعاً، وعند المعتزلة عقلاً، وجوزه الحشوية إما لعدم دليل الامتناع، وإما لما سيجيء من شبه الوقوع. وكذا عن الصغائر المنفرة لإخلالها بالدعوة إلى الإتباع. ولهذا ذهب كثير من المعتزلة إلى نفي الكبائر قبل البعثة أيضاً، وبعض الشيعة إلى نفي الصغائر ولو سهواً. والمذهب عندنا منع الكبائر بعد البعثة مطلقاً، والصغائر عمداً لا سهواً، لكن لا يصرون ولا يقرون بل ينبهون فيتنبهون، وذهب إمام الحرمين منا وأبو هاشم من المعتزلة إلى تجويز الصغائر عمداً.
On the infallibility of prophets, and it has preceded that the miracle necessitates truthfulness in the claim of prophethood and what pertains to it of conveying and the legality of rulings. So what is fancied to occur from prophets of ugly deeds is either contradictory to what the miracle necessitates, like lying regarding conveying, or not. The second is either disbelief or other disobedience, and it is either a major sin like murder and adultery, or a repulsive minor sin like stealing a morsel and cheating in measure by a grain, or a non-repulsive minor sin like a lie or intending a sin. All of that is either intentional or inadvertent, and after prophethood or before it. The majority (al-jumhur) hold the necessity of their infallibility from what contradicts the requisite of the miracle, and al-Qadi permitted it inadvertently, claiming it does not enter into the attestation intended by the miracle, and [they hold it] from disbelief; and the Azariqa of the Khawarij permitted it based on their permission of sin with their saying that every sin is disbelief; and the Shi'a permitted displaying it out of dissimulation (taqiyya) and caution against casting oneself into destruction, and it was answered that the most appropriate time for dissimulation is the beginning of the call due to the weakness of the caller and the strength of the opponent. And likewise [they hold it] from intentional major sins after prophethood; according to us (Ash'aris) by transmitted proof, and according to the Mu'tazila by rational proof; and the Hashwiyya permitted it either due to lack of evidence of impossibility, or due to what will come of the semblance of occurrence. And likewise from repulsive minor sins because they impair the call to following. Hence many of the Mu'tazila held the negation of major sins before prophethood as well, and some of the Shi'a held the negation of minor sins even inadvertently. And the school (madhhab) according to us is the prevention of major sins after prophethood absolutely, and of minor sins intentionally but not inadvertently, however they do not persist nor are they approved, rather they are admonished and so they become alert. And Imam al-Haramayn from us and Abu Hashim from the Mu'tazila held the permissibility of minor sins intentionally.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a classification of sins and a statement of the Ash'ari position on prophetic infallibility. It begins by affirming that miracles prove the prophet's truthfulness. Then it categorizes possible sins: those contradicting the miracle (like lying in conveying), and others (disbelief, major sins, repulsive minor sins, non-repulsive minor sins). It also distinguishes by intentionality and timing. It then reports the views of different groups: the majority (including Ash'aris) require infallibility from contradiction; al-Qadi permitted inadvertent sins; Azariqa permitted all sins (since they consider every sin kufr); Shi'a permitted taqiyya; Hashwiyya permitted due to no evidence; Mu'tazila held rational proof. The Ash'ari school ('indana) holds that prophets are protected from major sins absolutely after prophethood, and from minor sins intentionally but not inadvertently (though they do not persist). Some like Imam al-Haramayn and Abu Hashim allowed minor sins intentionally.

Key Terms
عصمة
معجزة
كبيرة
صغيرة
منفرة
سهو
عمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Taftazani's classification, which of the following is NOT a category of sin mentioned?
A) A sin that contradicts the miracle
B) A sin that is a major sin
C) A sin that is a repulsive minor sin
D) A sin that is a venial sin

Key Takeaway
The classification of sins according to their relation to the miracle and their nature provides the foundation for understanding prophetic infallibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that even a 'non-repulsive' minor sin like a lie is possible for a prophet only before prophethood or inadvertently after it, does that change how seriously you take your own minor sins? How will you guard against even the 'smallest' of lies today?
?
The passage distinguishes between a sin that contradicts the miracle (like false teaching) and one that does not. Is there any area of your life where you claim to follow the Prophet but your actions contradict the message? What one specific habit will you change this week to align better?
?
If the prophets are protected from repulsive minor sins like stealing a morsel, what does that say about the gravity of dishonesty in small matters? Will you commit to being scrupulously honest in every transaction, even those that seem insignificant?

The Ash'ari Position on Prophetic Infallibility
Al-Taftazani lists positions on infallibility and states the Ash'ari madhhab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari doctrine on prophetic infallibility and how it relates to other sects' positions.

Core Idea
Ash'aris affirm infallibility from major sins absolutely and from intentional minor sins.

After presenting the classification of sins, al-Taftazani now surveys the views of various Muslim groups on prophetic infallibility. He then clarifies the Ash'ari position, which strikes a middle ground: prophets are protected from major sins entirely and from minor sins when intentional, but inadvertent minor sins are possible, though they do not persist.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the sequence: opinions of al-Qadi, Azariqa, Shi'a, Hashwiyya, Mu'tazila, then the Ash'ari view.
The passage ends with the dissenting view of Imam al-Haramayn and Abu Hashim.
2
Identify the main positions
List the groups mentioned: majority (jumhur), al-Qadi, Azariqa, Shi'a, Hashwiyya, Mu'tazila, and the Ash'ari school. Note what each permits or denies.
Some groups permit sins that others deny.
3
Focus on the Ash'ari view
Find the sentence starting with 'والمذهب عندنا' – this is the authoritative stance according to Sunni Islam. It says: prevention of major sins absolutely, prevention of minor sins intentionally but not inadvertently, and that prophets are alerted and do not persist.
This is the key takeaway for Ash'ari theology.
4
Understand the justification
Notice the reasons given: for major sins, the proof is transmitted (sam'an) for Ash'aris and rational for Mu'tazila. For repulsive minor sins, they impair the call.
5
Note the minority opinion
Imam al-Haramayn and Abu Hashim allowed minor sins intentionally. This shows there was internal debate.
This is a dissenting view within Ash'ari circles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في عصمة الأنبياء، وقد سبق أن المعجزة تقتضي الصدق في دعوى النبوة وما يتعلق بها من التبليغ، وشرعية الأحكام. فما يتوهم صدوره عن الأنبياء من القبائح إما أن يكون منافياً لما يقتضيه المعجزة كالكذب فيما يتعلق بالتبليغ أو لا. والثاني إما أن يكون كفراً ومعصية غيره، وهي إما أن تكون كبيرة كالقتل والزنا، أو صغيرة منفرة كسرقة لقمة، والتطفيف بحبة. أو غير منفرة ككذبة، وهم بمعصية. كل ذلك إما عمداً أو سهواً، وبعد البعثة أو قبلها. والجمهور على وجوب عصمتهم عما ينافي مقتضى المعجزة، وقد جوزه القاضي سهواً زعماً منه أنه لا يدخل في التصديق المقصود بالمعجزة وعن الكفر، وقد جوزه الأزارقة من الخوارج بناء على تجويزهم الذنب مع قولهم بأن كل ذنب كفر، وجوز الشيعة إظهاره تقية واحترازاً عن إلقاء النفس في التهلكة ورد بأن أولى الأوقات بالتقية ابتداع الدعوة لضعف الداعي، وشوكة المخالف وكذا عن تعمد الكبائر بعد البعثة، فعندنا سمعاً، وعند المعتزلة عقلاً، وجوزه الحشوية إما لعدم دليل الامتناع، وإما لما سيجيء من شبه الوقوع. وكذا عن الصغائر المنفرة لإخلالها بالدعوة إلى الإتباع. ولهذا ذهب كثير من المعتزلة إلى نفي الكبائر قبل البعثة أيضاً، وبعض الشيعة إلى نفي الصغائر ولو سهواً. والمذهب عندنا منع الكبائر بعد البعثة مطلقاً، والصغائر عمداً لا سهواً، لكن لا يصرون ولا يقرون بل ينبهون فيتنبهون، وذهب إمام الحرمين منا وأبو هاشم من المعتزلة إلى تجويز الصغائر عمداً.
On the infallibility of prophets, and it has preceded that the miracle necessitates truthfulness in the claim of prophethood and what pertains to it of conveying and the legality of rulings. So what is fancied to occur from prophets of ugly deeds is either contradictory to what the miracle necessitates, like lying regarding conveying, or not. The second is either disbelief or other disobedience, and it is either a major sin like murder and adultery, or a repulsive minor sin like stealing a morsel and cheating in measure by a grain, or a non-repulsive minor sin like a lie or intending a sin. All of that is either intentional or inadvertent, and after prophethood or before it. The majority (al-jumhur) hold the necessity of their infallibility from what contradicts the requisite of the miracle, and al-Qadi permitted it inadvertently, claiming it does not enter into the attestation intended by the miracle, and [they hold it] from disbelief; and the Azariqa of the Khawarij permitted it based on their permission of sin with their saying that every sin is disbelief; and the Shi'a permitted displaying it out of dissimulation (taqiyya) and caution against casting oneself into destruction, and it was answered that the most appropriate time for dissimulation is the beginning of the call due to the weakness of the caller and the strength of the opponent. And likewise [they hold it] from intentional major sins after prophethood; according to us (Ash'aris) by transmitted proof, and according to the Mu'tazila by rational proof; and the Hashwiyya permitted it either due to lack of evidence of impossibility, or due to what will come of the semblance of occurrence. And likewise from repulsive minor sins because they impair the call to following. Hence many of the Mu'tazila held the negation of major sins before prophethood as well, and some of the Shi'a held the negation of minor sins even inadvertently. And the school (madhhab) according to us is the prevention of major sins after prophethood absolutely, and of minor sins intentionally but not inadvertently, however they do not persist nor are they approved, rather they are admonished and so they become alert. And Imam al-Haramayn from us and Abu Hashim from the Mu'tazila held the permissibility of minor sins intentionally.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a classification of sins and a statement of the Ash'ari position on prophetic infallibility. It begins by affirming that miracles prove the prophet's truthfulness. Then it categorizes possible sins: those contradicting the miracle (like lying in conveying), and others (disbelief, major sins, repulsive minor sins, non-repulsive minor sins). It also distinguishes by intentionality and timing. It then reports the views of different groups: the majority (including Ash'aris) require infallibility from contradiction; al-Qadi permitted inadvertent sins; Azariqa permitted all sins (since they consider every sin kufr); Shi'a permitted taqiyya; Hashwiyya permitted due to no evidence; Mu'tazila held rational proof. The Ash'ari school ('indana) holds that prophets are protected from major sins absolutely after prophethood, and from minor sins intentionally but not inadvertently (though they do not persist). Some like Imam al-Haramayn and Abu Hashim allowed minor sins intentionally.

Key Terms
عصمة
سهو

تقية

أزارقة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Ash'aris believe prophets are absolutely sinless, including inadvertent minor sins.
Correction: The Ash'ari school actually allows inadvertent minor sins, though prophets do not persist in them.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari school, which sins are impossible for prophets after prophethood?
A) All sins, major and minor, intentional and inadvertent.
B) Major sins absolutely, and minor sins intentionally, but not inadvertent minor sins.
C) Only major sins intentionally.
D) Sins that contradict the miracle.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari position balances infallibility: prophets are protected from major sins and intentional minor sins, but inadvertent minor sins are possible, though they are immediately corrected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet (peace be upon him) never committed a major sin intentionally, yet you sometimes fall into them without immediate remorse, how does your own relationship with repentance compare to the prophetic example of being instantly admonished and becoming alert? Do you truly fear the consequences of your sins, or do you hope for forgiveness without real change? What will you do today to immediately turn back from a recurring sin?
?
You trust the Qur'an and Sunnah completely. But if the prophets could make inadvertent minor mistakes (as Ash'aris hold), does that ever make you doubt the reliability of the revelation? Or does the fact that they were immediately corrected strengthen your trust? In your daily life, do you treat the prophetic commands as absolutely reliable, or do you sometimes rationalize disobedience? Identify one command you have been neglecting and commit to acting on it this week.
?
The passage refutes the Shi'a argument for taqiyya by saying the best time for dissimulation is at the beginning of the call, when the prophet is weak. Think of a time when you hid your faith or compromised your values out of fear. Was that fear truly life-threatening, or just discomfort? The prophets faced real danger but never hid the truth after their call was established. Will you take a concrete step to be more open about your beliefs, knowing that God is with you? What specific situation will you face tomorrow where you can stand firm?

Proof from Necessary Consequences: Why Prophets Cannot Sin
Al-Taftazani proves prophetic infallibility by five impossible consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Taftazani uses a logical argument of impossible consequences to prove that prophets are protected from sin.

Core Idea
If prophets could sin, impossible consequences would follow—so they are infallible.

Al-Taftazani presents a powerful argument: if prophets committed sins, then undeniable logical and religious consequences would follow. But all these consequences are impossible, so the premise must be false. This lesson unpacks the proof step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the four consequences
The passage lists four things that would be necessary if prophets sinned. Find each one and note the reason why it is negated.
The proof uses both consensus (ijma') and Quranic verses.
3
Understand the logical structure
Notice that the proof is a reductio ad absurdum: accept the premise (prophets sin) leads to contradictions with established truths, so the premise is false.
This is a common method in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لنا. أنه لو صدر عنهم الذنب لزم أمور كلها منتفية. الأول - حرمة اتباعهم. لكنه واجب بالإجماع، وبقوله تعالى: {قل إن كنتم تحبون الله فاتبعوني يحببكم الله}. الثاني - رد شهادتهم لقوله تعالى: {إن جاءكم فاسق...} الآية. والإجماع على ذلك، لكنه منتف للقطع بأن من يرد شهادته في القليل من متاع الدنيا لا يستحق القبول في أمر الدين القائم إلى يوم الدين. الثالث - وجوب منعهم وزجرهم لعموم أدلة الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر. لكنه منتف لاستلزامه إيذائهم المحرم بالإجماع، ولقوله تعالى: {والذين يؤذون الله ورسوله...} الآية. الرابع - استحقاقهم العذاب واللعن واللوم والذم لدخولهم تحت قوله تعالى: {ومن يعص الله ورسوله فإن له نار جهنم} وقوله {ألا لعنة الله على الظالمين} وقوله {لم تقولون ما لا تفعلون} وقوله {أتأمرون الناس بالبر وتنسون أنفسكم}. لكن ذلك منتف بالإجماع. ولكونه من أعظم المنفرات.
For us: If sin issued from them, then matters would necessarily follow, all of which are negated. First: the prohibition of following them. But it is obligatory by consensus and by His saying: {Say: If you love Allah, follow me, and Allah will love you}. Second: the rejection of their testimony — by His saying: {If a wicked person comes to you...} the verse. And consensus is upon that, but it is negated because it is certain that the one whose testimony is rejected regarding a small amount of worldly goods does not deserve acceptance in the matter of religion lasting to the Day of Judgment. Third: the obligation to prevent and rebuke them due to general proofs of commanding good and forbidding evil. But it is negated because it necessitates harming them, which is forbidden by consensus, and by His saying: {Those who harm Allah and His Messenger...} the verse. Fourth: their deserving punishment, curse, blame, and censure because they fall under His saying: {Whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, indeed for him is the fire of Hell}, and His saying {Indeed the curse of Allah is upon the wrongdoers}, and His saying {Why do you say what you do not do}, and His saying {Do you enjoin righteousness upon people while you forget yourselves?}. But that is negated by consensus, and because it is among the greatest repulsives.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents a logical proof (dalil) for prophetic infallibility. It argues that if prophets committed sins, four (or five, but four are enumerated here) necessary consequences would follow: (1) following them would be forbidden (ḥurma), but consensus and the Qur'an command following; (2) their testimony would be rejected, but accepting their testimony in religion is indispensable; (3) it would be obligatory to prevent and rebuke them (al-amr bi-l-ma'ruf), but that would harm them which is forbidden; (4) they would deserve punishment and blame, but by consensus prophets are free from such. Since these consequences are negated, the premise (that they sin) is false. The proof is based on consensus (ijma') and scriptural evidence.

Key Terms
لوازم
حرمة اتباع
رد شهادة
زجر
استحقاق عذاب
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof for prophetic infallibility relies only on consensus (ijma').
Correction: The proof also uses Quranic verses and logical necessity. Each consequence is supported by both consensus and scripture.

Checkpoint
According to this proof, which is NOT one of the consequences of prophets sinning?
A) Prohibition of following them.
B) Rejection of their testimony.
C) Invalidation of their prophethood.
D) Obligation to rebuke them.

Key Takeaway
Prophets are infallible because if they sinned, the results would contradict clear Quranic commands and consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that if the Prophet could sin, his testimony about even a small worldly matter would be rejected. How does this affect the way you receive his teachings on matters of eternal consequence? Are you as quick to obey his commands about daily life as you are about worship?
?
Imagine the Prophet being rebuked for a sin—would your heart not break? Yet Allah commanded us to follow him absolutely. Does your actual following reflect that absolute trust, or do you pick and choose? What would it take for you to follow him without reservation?
?
If you had to rely on this proof alone to convince someone of the Prophet's infallibility, would you be confident? What part of the argument do you find most compelling, and where do you feel your understanding needs strengthening to defend this core belief?

The Ash'ari Position on Prophetic Minor Sins
Al-Sanūsī enumerates theological positions on prophetic minor sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different theological positions on whether prophets can commit minor sins after their mission, especially the Ash'ari view.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from minor sins intentionally, but not from forgetful slips.

The issue of prophetic infallibility (ʿiṣma) is a cornerstone of Islamic theology. While all Muslims agree that prophets are protected from major sins, there is debate about minor sins. In this passage, al-Sanūsī lays out the various schools' stances, clarifying the Ash'ari position that prophets are not permitted to commit minor sins intentionally but are warned if they do so forgetfully.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the passage and note the views of the Mu'tazila, Shi'a, and the Ash'ari school regarding minor sins.
The passage also mentions a dissenting view within the Ash'ari school.
2
Understand the key distinction
Notice the difference between 'amdan (intentional) and sahw (forgetful). The Ash'ari view distinguishes between these.
3
See the starting point of the argument
The passage ends with 'lā nahū' indicating that the proof against sinning will follow. Prepare to engage with the eight arguments in the next lesson.

السادس - كونهم غير مخلصين، لأن المذنب قد أغواه الشيطان ، والمخلص ليس كذلك لقوله تعالى حكاية: ﴿وَلأُغْوِيَنَّهُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ إِلَّا عِبَادَكَ مِنْهُمُ الْمُخْلِصِينَ ) (٢). لكن اللازم منتف بالإجماع. وبقوله تعالى في إبراهيم ويعقوب : إِنَّـا أَخْلَصْنَاهُمْ بِخالِصَةٍ ذِكْرَى الدَّارِ ﴾ (٣) . وفي يوسف: إنّه مِنْ عِبادِنا المُخلصين (٤)

And likewise regarding the minor sins that repel (people) because they impair the call to following (the prophet). Therefore many of the Mu'tazila held to denial of major sins before the mission as well, and some of the Shi'a to denial of minor sins even if forgetfully. The school with us is prohibition of major sins after the mission absolutely, and of minor sins intentionally not forgetfully, but they do not persist nor are they confirmed, rather they are warned and they become heedful. And Imam al-Haramayn among us and Abu Hashim among the Mu'tazila held to permitting minor sins intentionally. For us: if sin were to occur from them, then matters would follow, all of which are negated.
First - the prohibition of following them. But it is obligatory by consensus, and by His statement: {Say: If you love Allah, then follow me, Allah will love you} (3:31).
Second - rejection of their testimony - due to His statement: {If a sinner comes to you...} (49:6) the verse. And consensus on that, but it is negated because it is certain that the one whose testimony is rejected in the little of worldly goods does not deserve acceptance in the matter of religion lasting until the Day of Judgment.
Third - the obligation of preventing them and rebuking them due to the generality of evidences for commanding good and forbidding evil. But it is negated because it necessitates harming them, which is prohibited by consensus, and due to His statement: {And those who harm Allah and His Messenger...} (9:61) the verse.
Fourth - their deserving punishment, curse, blame, and censure because they fall under His statement: {And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, then indeed for him is the fire of Hell} (72:23) and His statement: {Indeed the curse of Allah is upon the wrongdoers} (11:18) and His statement: {Why do you say what you do not do?} (61:2) and His statement: {Do you enjoin righteousness upon people while you forget yourselves?} (2:44). But that is negated by consensus. And because it is among the greatest repellants.
Fifth - their not attaining the covenant of prophethood due to His statement: {My covenant does not reach the wrongdoers} (2:124). For what is meant by it is prophethood or the imamate which is below it.
Sixth - their being not sincere (mukhlis), because the sinner may have been seduced by Satan, and the sincere one is not like that due to His statement relating: {And I will surely seduce them all, except Your sincere servants among them} (15:39-40). But the necessary consequence is negated by consensus. And by His statement regarding Abraham and Jacob: {Indeed We purified them with a pure quality, the remembrance of the abode} (38:46). And regarding Joseph: {Indeed he was among Our sincere servants} (12:24).
Seventh - their being of the party (hizb) of Satan and his followers. And the necessary consequence is absolutely false.
Eighth - their not being hastening in good deeds and counted with Allah among the chosen good ones, for there is no good in sin, but the necessary consequence is negated due to His statement regarding some of them: {Indeed they used to hasten in good deeds} (21:90) and {And indeed they are with Us among the chosen good ones} (38:47). And the obtaining of the desired from these aspects is a subject of investigation, because the obligation of following is only concerning the Sharia and conveying of rulings, and in summary concerning what is not a slip or a natural disposition; and deserving punishment and rejection of testimony is only due to a major sin, or persistence in a minor sin without repentance and return; and the necessity of rebuke and prevention and deserving punishment and blame is only on the supposition of intentionality and lack of repentance; and with that the prophet is not harmed, rather he rejoices; and by mere major sin forgetfully or minor sin even intentionally, a person is not counted among the wrongdoers absolutely, nor among those whom Satan seduced, nor from the party of Satan, especially with repentance; and upon the universality of good deeds for every...
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage discusses prophetic infallibility ('isma) specifically regarding minor sins (sagha'ir). The author begins by noting that minor sins that repel followers are also denied because they impair the call. He then summarizes positions: many Mu'tazila deny even major sins before prophethood; some Shi'a deny minor sins even if forgetful; the Sunni (Ash'ari) position is that major sins are prohibited absolutely after prophethood, and minor sins only if intentional, not if forgetful, but prophets are warned and they heed. Some scholars like Imam al-Haramayn and Abu Hashim allowed minor sins intentionally. The author then presents eight arguments (luzum) that would follow if prophets sinned, each argued to be false (muntafi) by consensus or explicit scriptural evidence. The first: following them would be prohibited, but it is obligatory. The second: their testimony would be rejected, but such rejection is for worldly matters, not religious ones. The third: we would have to rebuke them, but that would harm them, which is prohibited. The fourth: they would deserve punishment, curse, etc., but this is repugnant and false by consensus. The fifth: they would not attain the covenant of prophethood (interpreted as prophethood or imamate). The sixth: they would not be sincere servants (mukhlis), yet the Qur'an affirms sincerity for some prophets. The seventh: they would be of Satan's party, which is clearly false. The eighth: they would not be hastening in good deeds, yet the Qur'an says some prophets did. After listing these eight, the author provides a more nuanced rebuttal: the obligation to follow concerns only the Sharia and its transmission, not every personal slip; punishment and rejection of testimony apply only to major sins or persistence in minor sins without repentance; rebuke and punishment only on intentionality and lack of repentance; and even if a sin occurs (forgetfully or even intentionally with repentance), it does not make one absolutely a wrongdoer or of Satan's party. The passage ends mid-sentence discussing universality of good deeds, continuing the argument.

Key Terms
الصغائر
الكبائر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Ash'ari school permits all minor sins.
Correction: They prohibit intentional minor sins but allow forgetful ones, and prophets are quickly warned.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari school, are prophets permitted to commit minor sins intentionally after their mission?
A) Yes, they are permitted.
B) No, they are prohibited.
C) Only if forgetful.
D) It depends on the sin.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari school prohibits prophets from committing minor sins intentionally after prophethood, but allows forgetful slips which are quickly corrected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If prophets are held to such a high standard that even intentional minor sins are prohibited, how do you justify your own casual attitude toward what you consider 'small' sins? What would it look like for you to treat every sin as a serious offense against your relationship with Allah?
?
The passage says prophets, when they slip forgetfully, are immediately warned and become heedful. When you fall into sin, do you instantly turn back to Allah or do you let it linger? What is the one sin you have been persisting in that you know you need to repent from right now?
?
The Ash'ari position protects the prophetic call from being repelled by sin. Are there any sins in your life that might be pushing others away from the truth of Islam? Which one are you most aware of, and what will you do about it today?

Eight Consequences of Prophetic Sin and Their Refutation
Al-Sanūsī presents eight necessary consequences of prophetic sin and refutes them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the eight logical consequences that would arise if prophets sinned, and how each is refuted.

Core Idea
If prophets sinned, it would contradict their infallibility, leading to impossibilities.

After establishing the positions on minor sins, al-Sanūsī provides a comprehensive argument by examining eight hypothetical consequences (luzūm) that would follow if prophets were to commit sins. Each consequence is shown to be false, thereby confirming the necessity of prophetic infallibility. This structured argument is a classic example of kalām reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the eight arguments
Go through each of the eight consequences listed (from 'الأول' to 'الثامن') and note the scriptural or rational proof given for each.
Each argument follows the pattern: if sin, then X; but X is false; therefore sin cannot occur.
2
Understand the rebuttal
After the eight arguments, al-Sanūsī offers a qualifying rebuttal that specifies the conditions under which some consequences would not apply.
He argues that obligation to follow is only regarding sharia transmission, not personal slips.
3
Connect to infallibility
Observe how this cumulative argument strengthens the doctrine of ʿiṣma by showing that sinning would entail unacceptable outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا عن الصغائر المنفرة لإخلالها بالدعوة إلى الإتباع . ولهذا ذهب كثير من المعتزلة إلى نفي الكبائر قبل البعثة أيضاً، وبعض الشيعة إلى نفي الصغائر ولو سهواً . والمذهب عندنا منع الكبائر بعد البعثة مطلقاً، والصغائر عمداً لا سهواً، لكن لا يصرون ولا يقرون بل ينبهون فيتنبهون، وذهب إمام الحرمين منا وأبـو هاشم من المعتزلة إلى تجويز الصغائر عمداً لنا . أنه لو صدر عنهم الذنب لزم أمور كلها منتفية .
الأول - حرمة اتباعهم . لكنه واجب بالإجماع، وبقوله تعالى : ﴿قُلْ إنْ كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ اللهَ فَاتَّبِعُونِي يُحْيِيكُم الله ) (۱).
الثاني - رد شهادتهم - لقوله تعالى : إِنْ جَاءَكُم فَاسِقٌ ... ) (۲) الآية . والإجماع على ذلك، لكنه منتف للقطع بأن من يرد شهادته في القليل من متاع الدنيا لا يستحق القبول في أمر الدين القائم إلى يوم الدين .
الثالث - وجوب منعهم وزجرهم لعموم أدلة الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر. لكنه منتف لاستلزامه إيذائهم المحرم بالإجماع، ولقوله تعالى: ﴿والَّذِينَ يُؤْذُونَ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ . . . (٣) الآية .
الرابع - استحقاقهم العذاب واللعن واللوم والذم لدخولهم تحت قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ فَإِنَّ لَهُ نَارَ جَهَنَّمَ ) (٤) وقوله (ألا لعنة الله عَلَى اللَّهِ الظَّالِمِينَ) (٥) وقوله : لِمَ تَقُولُونَ مَا لَا تَفْعَلُونَ ) (۱) وقوله : (أَتَأْمُرُونَ النَّاسَ بِالْبِرِّ وَتَنْسَوْنَ أَنْفُسَكُمْ ) . لكن ذلك منتف بالإجماع . ولكونه من أعظم المنفرات .
الخامس - عدم نيلهم عهد النبوة لقوله تعالى : ولا ينال عهدي الظالمين فإن المراد به النبوة أو الإمامة التي دونها .
السادس - كونهم غير مخلصين، لأن المذنب قد أغواه الشيطان ، والمخلص ليس كذلك لقوله تعالى حكاية: ﴿وَلأُغْوِيَنَّهُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ إِلَّا عِبَادَكَ مِنْهُمُ الْمُخْلِصِينَ ) (٢). لكن اللازم منتف بالإجماع. وبقوله تعالى في إبراهيم ويعقوب : إِنَّـا أَخْلَصْنَاهُمْ بِخالِصَةٍ ذِكْرَى الدَّارِ ﴾ (٣) . وفي يوسف: إنّه مِنْ عِبادِنا المُخلصين (٤)
السابع - كونهم من حزب الشيطان ومتبعيه. واللازم قطعي البطلان .
الثامن - عدم كونهم مسارعين في الخيرات ومعدودين عند الله من المصطفين الأخيار، إذ لا خير في الذنب، لكن اللازم منتف لقوله تعالى في حق بعضهم: ﴿إِنَّهُمْ كَانُوا يُسَارِعُونَ فِي الْخَيْرَاتِ) (). ﴿وَإِنَّهُمْ عِنْدَنَا لَمِنَ الْمُصْطَفَيْن الأخيار) (٦) . وحصول المطلوب من هذه الوجوه محل بحث، لأن وجوب الاتباع إنما هو فيما يتعلق بالشريعة وتبليغ الأحكام، وبالجملة فيما ليس بزلة ولا طبع واستحقاق العذاب، ورد الشهادة إنما يكون بكبيرة ، أو إصرار على صغيرة من غير إنابة و رجوع، ولزوم الزجر والمنع واستحقاق العذاب واللوم إنما هو على تقدير التعمد وعدم الإنابة، ومع ذلك فلا يتأذى به النبي، بل يبتهج وبمجرد كبيرة سهواً أو صغيرة ولو عمداً لا يعد المرء من الظالمين على الإطلاق، ولا من الذين أغواهم الشيطان ، ولا من حزب الشيطان، سيما مع الإنابة، وعلى كون الخيرات لعموم كل
And likewise regarding the minor sins that repel (people) because they impair the call to following (the prophet). Therefore many of the Mu'tazila held to denial of major sins before the mission as well, and some of the Shi'a to denial of minor sins even if forgetfully. The school with us is prohibition of major sins after the mission absolutely, and of minor sins intentionally not forgetfully, but they do not persist nor are they confirmed, rather they are warned and they become heedful. And Imam al-Haramayn among us and Abu Hashim among the Mu'tazila held to permitting minor sins intentionally. For us: if sin were to occur from them, then matters would follow, all of which are negated.
First - the prohibition of following them. But it is obligatory by consensus, and by His statement: {Say: If you love Allah, then follow me, Allah will love you} (3:31).
Second - rejection of their testimony - due to His statement: {If a sinner comes to you...} (49:6) the verse. And consensus on that, but it is negated because it is certain that the one whose testimony is rejected in the little of worldly goods does not deserve acceptance in the matter of religion lasting until the Day of Judgment.
Third - the obligation of preventing them and rebuking them due to the generality of evidences for commanding good and forbidding evil. But it is negated because it necessitates harming them, which is prohibited by consensus, and due to His statement: {And those who harm Allah and His Messenger...} (9:61) the verse.
Fourth - their deserving punishment, curse, blame, and censure because they fall under His statement: {And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, then indeed for him is the fire of Hell} (72:23) and His statement: {Indeed the curse of Allah is upon the wrongdoers} (11:18) and His statement: {Why do you say what you do not do?} (61:2) and His statement: {Do you enjoin righteousness upon people while you forget yourselves?} (2:44). But that is negated by consensus. And because it is among the greatest repellants.
Fifth - their not attaining the covenant of prophethood due to His statement: {My covenant does not reach the wrongdoers} (2:124). For what is meant by it is prophethood or the imamate which is below it.
Sixth - their being not sincere (mukhlis), because the sinner may have been seduced by Satan, and the sincere one is not like that due to His statement relating: {And I will surely seduce them all, except Your sincere servants among them} (15:39-40). But the necessary consequence is negated by consensus. And by His statement regarding Abraham and Jacob: {Indeed We purified them with a pure quality, the remembrance of the abode} (38:46). And regarding Joseph: {Indeed he was among Our sincere servants} (12:24).
Seventh - their being of the party (hizb) of Satan and his followers. And the necessary consequence is absolutely false.
Eighth - their not being hastening in good deeds and counted with Allah among the chosen good ones, for there is no good in sin, but the necessary consequence is negated due to His statement regarding some of them: {Indeed they used to hasten in good deeds} (21:90) and {And indeed they are with Us among the chosen good ones} (38:47). And the obtaining of the desired from these aspects is a subject of investigation, because the obligation of following is only concerning the Sharia and conveying of rulings, and in summary concerning what is not a slip or a natural disposition; and deserving punishment and rejection of testimony is only due to a major sin, or persistence in a minor sin without repentance and return; and the necessity of rebuke and prevention and deserving punishment and blame is only on the supposition of intentionality and lack of repentance; and with that the prophet is not harmed, rather he rejoices; and by mere major sin forgetfully or minor sin even intentionally, a person is not counted among the wrongdoers absolutely, nor among those whom Satan seduced, nor from the party of Satan, especially with repentance; and upon the universality of good deeds for every...
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage discusses prophetic infallibility ('isma) specifically regarding minor sins (sagha'ir). The author begins by noting that minor sins that repel followers are also denied because they impair the call. He then summarizes positions: many Mu'tazila deny even major sins before prophethood; some Shi'a deny minor sins even if forgetful; the Sunni (Ash'ari) position is that major sins are prohibited absolutely after prophethood, and minor sins only if intentional, not if forgetful, but prophets are warned and they heed. Some scholars like Imam al-Haramayn and Abu Hashim allowed minor sins intentionally. The author then presents eight arguments (luzum) that would follow if prophets sinned, each argued to be false (muntafi) by consensus or explicit scriptural evidence. The first: following them would be prohibited, but it is obligatory. The second: their testimony would be rejected, but such rejection is for worldly matters, not religious ones. The third: we would have to rebuke them, but that would harm them, which is prohibited. The fourth: they would deserve punishment, curse, etc., but this is repugnant and false by consensus. The fifth: they would not attain the covenant of prophethood (interpreted as prophethood or imamate). The sixth: they would not be sincere servants (mukhlis), yet the Qur'an affirms sincerity for some prophets. The seventh: they would be of Satan's party, which is clearly false. The eighth: they would not be hastening in good deeds, yet the Qur'an says some prophets did. After listing these eight, the author provides a more nuanced rebuttal: the obligation to follow concerns only the Sharia and its transmission, not every personal slip; punishment and rejection of testimony apply only to major sins or persistence in minor sins without repentance; rebuke and punishment only on intentionality and lack of repentance; and even if a sin occurs (forgetfully or even intentionally with repentance), it does not make one absolutely a wrongdoer or of Satan's party. The passage ends mid-sentence discussing universality of good deeds, continuing the argument.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that any sin by a prophet automatically leads to all eight consequences.
Correction: The author explains they are conditional on intentionality and lack of repentance; minor sins with repentance do not incur these consequences.

Checkpoint
What is the first consequence listed by al-Sanūsī if a prophet commits a sin?
A) The prophet would lose his status as a prophet.
B) Following the prophet would become prohibited.
C) The prophet would be punished immediately.
D) The prophet would be considered a sinner.

Key Takeaway
The eight arguments demonstrate that prophetic sin would lead to absurdities, confirming the necessity of ʿiṣma, but the consequences are conditional on intentionality and lack of repentance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read that prophets are infallible so that they can be followed without hesitation. Look at your own life: are there areas where your actions contradict what you call others to? If someone followed you in every detail, would they be led closer to Allah or further away? What will you change today to make yourself more worthy of being followed?
?
The source says that a prophet rejoices even when rebuked, because he is innocent. Think of the last time someone corrected you. Did you feel anger, defensiveness, or rejection? Or did you welcome it as a means of growth? Your reaction reveals whether you love the truth more than your own ego. What step will you take this week to embrace correction with humility?
?
The eighth consequence shows that a person who sins cannot be described as 'hastening in good deeds.' But the Qur'an says prophets did. Examine your own day: are you hastening towards good, or are you procrastinating and delaying obedience? If you were to die tonight, would Allah count you among those who eagerly race to good deeds? What is holding you back right now?

Why Arguments for Prophetic Sinlessness Are Not Decisive
Lists and critiques four arguments for prophetic sinlessness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four scriptural arguments used to argue that prophets cannot commit major sins and why these arguments are considered inconclusive by scholars.

Core Idea
Scriptural arguments for prophetic sinlessness are strong but not absolute; they leave room for minor sins and forgetfulness.

In this lesson, we examine four key arguments that are often used to prove that prophets are protected from major sins. These arguments rely on Quranic verses about the covenant of prophethood, sincerity, allegiance to Satan, and being among the elite. The author presents them and then offers a critical analysis showing that they do not decisively exclude the possibility of minor sins or sins done forgetfully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
First, read the full Arabic passage and its literal translation to get a sense of the author's flow and the four arguments presented.
Note the Quranic citations as they are central to each argument.
2
Identify the four arguments
Identify the fifth, sixth, seventh, and eighth arguments. For each, note the Quranic proof and the author's initial presentation.
The arguments are: covenant of prophethood, sincerity, party of Satan, and hastening in good deeds.
3
Understand the critique
Read the critique section carefully. The author explains why the necessary consequences do not follow absolutely, focusing on the role of forgetfulness, repentance, and the distinction between major and minor sins.
The author concludes that these arguments are open to discussion and not decisive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس - عدم نيلهم عهد النبوة لقوله تعالى : ولا ينال عهدي الظالمين فإن المراد به النبوة أو الإمامة التي دونها . (1) السادس - كونهم غير مخلصين، لأن المذنب قد أغواه الشيطان ، والمخلص ليس كذلك لقوله تعالى حكاية: ﴿وَلأُغْوِيَنَّهُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ إِلَّا عِبَادَكَ مِنْهُمُ الْمُخْلِصِينَ ) (٢). لكن اللازم منتف بالإجماع. وبقوله تعالى في إبراهيم ويعقوب : إِنَّـا أَخْلَصْنَاهُمْ بِخالِصَةٍ ذِكْرَى الدَّارِ ﴾ (٣) . وفي يوسف: إنّه مِنْ عِبادِنا المُخلصين (٤) السابع - كونهم من حزب الشيطان ومتبعيه. واللازم قطعي البطلان . الثامن - عدم كونهم مسارعين في الخيرات ومعدودين عند الله من المصطفين الأخيار، إذ لا خير في الذنب، لكن اللازم منتف لقوله تعالى في حق بعضهم: ﴿إِنَّهُمْ كَانُوا يُسَارِعُونَ فِي الْخَيْرَاتِ) (). ﴿وَإِنَّهُمْ عِنْدَنَا لَمِنَ الْمُصْطَفَيْن الأخيار) (٦) . وحصول المطلوب من هذه الوجوه محل بحث، لأن وجوب الاتباع إنما هو فيما يتعلق بالشريعة وتبليغ الأحكام، وبالجملة فيما ليس بزلة ولا طبع واستحقاق العذاب، ورد الشهادة إنما يكون بكبيرة ، أو إصرار على صغيرة من غير إنابة و رجوع، ولزوم الزجر والمنع واستحقاق العذاب واللوم إنما هو على تقدير التعمد وعدم الإنابة، ومع ذلك فلا يتأذى به النبي، بل يبتهج وبمجرد كبيرة سهواً أو صغيرة ولو عمداً لا يعد المرء من الظالمين على الإطلاق، ولا من الذين أغواهم الشيطان ، ولا من حزب الشيطان، سيما مع الإنابة، وعلى كون الخيرات لعموم كل فعل وترك . فمسارعة البعض إليها أو كونه من زمرة الأخيار لا ينافي صدور ذنب عن آخر سيما سهواً أو مع التوبة (١) . وبالجملة فدلالة الوجوه المذكورة على نفي الكبيرة سهواً، أو الصغيرة الغير المنفر عمداً على ما هو المتنازع محل نظر
Fifth: Their not attaining the covenant of prophethood because of His statement: 'My covenant does not reach the wrongdoers' (Quran 2:124) – for what is meant by it is prophethood or the imamate below it. Sixth: Their not being sincere, because the sinner may have been seduced by Satan, while the sincere is not like that, as per His statement narrating: 'I will surely seduce them all, except Your sincere servants among them' (Quran 15:39-40). But the necessary consequence is negated by consensus. And by His statement concerning Abraham and Jacob: 'Indeed, We purified them with a pure quality: remembrance of the Home' (Quran 38:46). And concerning Joseph: 'Indeed, he was of Our sincere servants' (Quran 12:24). Seventh: Their being of the party of Satan and his followers – and the necessary consequence is definitely false. Eighth: Their not being hastening in good deeds and counted among Allah's chosen elite, for there is no good in sin, but the necessary consequence is negated by His statement concerning some of them: 'Indeed, they used to hasten in good deeds' (Quran 21:90) and 'Indeed, they are with Us among the chosen elite' (Quran 38:47). Yet attaining the desired from these points is open to discussion, because the obligation of following is only concerning what relates to the Law and conveying rulings, and in sum concerning what is not a slip or a natural disposition deserving punishment; rejection of testimony is only due to a major sin or persistence in a minor sin without repentance and return; the necessity of rebuke and prevention and deserving punishment and blame is only on the assumption of deliberation and lack of repentance; and despite that, the prophet is not harmed, but rather rejoices. By merely a major sin forgetfully or a minor sin even deliberately, a person is not counted as a wrongdoer absolutely, nor among those whom Satan seduced, nor of Satan's party, especially with repentance. And that good deeds encompass all actions and omissions, so some hastening to them or being among the group of the elite does not contradict the occurrence of a sin from another, especially forgetfully or with repentance. In sum, the indication of these mentioned points for negating a major sin forgetfully, or a minor sin that is not repugnant deliberately, concerning what is disputed, is questionable.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage continues a discussion on prophetic sinlessness (عصمة الأنبياء). It lists the fifth through eighth arguments used to prove that prophets cannot commit major sins, followed by a critique showing these arguments are not decisive. The author first presents each argument: (fifth) that sinners cannot attain the covenant of prophethood; (sixth) that sinners are not among the sincere servants; (seventh) that sinners belong to Satan's party; (eighth) that sinners cannot be hastening in good works like the elite. For each, the author cites Quranic verses and then notes a counterpoint: e.g., the verse about sincerity is general, but the necessary consequence (that a sinning prophet cannot be sincere) is negated by consensus and by other verses showing that prophets are described as sincere despite their sin. The author then explains why these arguments are not conclusive: the obligation to obey and accept testimony only applies to matters of law, not slips; rebuke and punishment only occur if the sin is deliberate and without repentance; moreover, a person is not absolutely called a wrongdoer due to a single sin, especially if minor or with repentance. The author concludes that these points do not decisively prove the negation of major sin forgetfully or minor non-repugnant sin deliberately, leaving the matter open to discussion.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many believe that any sin from a prophet automatically negates his prophethood or makes him a wrongdoer absolutely.
Correction: The author shows that sin does not necessarily negate prophethood; it depends on factors such as whether the sin was deliberate or forgetful, major or minor, and whether repentance occurred.

Key Takeaway
The arguments for prophetic sinlessness are not absolute; they allow for minor sins and forgetfulness, especially with repentance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If even the prophets could commit minor sins and forgetfulness, how does that change the way you view your own repeated mistakes? Will you continue to despair over sins that Allah can forgive, or will you hasten to repentance as the prophets did?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim commit a sin, do you automatically label them as 'wrongdoers' beyond redemption, or do you remember that even the best of creation are not immune to slips? What does this lesson teach you about giving others the benefit of the doubt?
?
This lesson argues that the arguments for sinlessness are not decisive. How does that affect your understanding of the prophets' humanity and your own relationship with them? Are you willing to see them as real people who struggled, repented, and were still chosen by Allah?
