Transmitted Proofs and the Virtue-Superiority Distinction
Taftazani presents three transmitted proofs and replies that they show virtue, not superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Taftazani refutes scriptural proofs for angelic superiority by distinguishing between virtue (fadilah) and superiority (afdaliyyah), especially over prophets.

Core Idea
The angels' obedience proves their virtue, not their superiority over prophets.

After addressing the general argument, Taftazani turns to specific Quranic verses that seem to elevate angels. He shows that these verses only highlight their virtue, not absolute superiority, particularly over prophets. This lesson covers the first three verses and the key conceptual distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the three verses
Read the verses from an-Nahl (16:49-50), al-Anbiya (21:19-20), and al-Anbiya (21:26-28) that describe angels' humility, fear, and obedience.
Notice how each verse emphasizes a particular praiseworthy quality.
2
Understand the author's interpretation
The author argues that these descriptions indicate virtue (fadilah), not superiority (afdaliyyah).
3
Grasp the distinction
The key point is that while angels have these virtues, it does not mean they are superior to prophets, who have their own unique qualities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثامن - أن أعمالهم أكثر وأدوم وأقوم، وعلومهم أكمل وأكثر. وأجيب بأن المقرون بقهر المضاد وتحمل المشاق أدخل في استحقاق الثواب . ) . أيضاً بوجوه نقلية وعقلية، أما النقليات فمنها قوله تعالى: ﴿ والله يسجد ما في السموات وما في الأرض من دابة والملائكة وهم لايستكبرون . يخافون ربهم من فوقهم ويفعلون ما يؤمرون (1) خصصهم بالتواضع، وترك الاستكبار في السجود. وفيه إشارة إلى أن غيرهم ليس كذلك، وأن أسباب التكبر والتعظم حاصلة لهم، ووصفهم باستمرار الخوف وامتثال الأوامر ومن جملتها اجتناب المنهيات . ومنها قوله تعالى : " ومن عنده لا يستكبرون عن عبادته ولايستحسرون . يسبحون الليل والنهار لا يفترون) (۲) وصفهم بالقرب والشرف عنده وبالتواضع والمواظبة على الطاعة والتسبيح . ومنها قوله تعالى : بل عباد مكرمون لا يسبقونه بالقول وهم بأمره يعملون ) (۳) .. إلى أن قال: وهم من خشيته مشفقون. وخصهم بالكرامة المطلقة والامتثال والخشية وهذه الأمور أساس كافة الخيرات . والجواب أن جميع ذلك إنما يدل على فضيلتهم، لا أفضليتهم، سيما على الأنبياء، ومنها قوله تعالى: قل لا أقول لكم عندي خزائن الله ولا أعلم الغيب ولا أقول إني ملك (١) فإن مثل هذا الكلام إنما يحسن إذا كان الملك أفضل والجواب أنه إنما قال حين استعجله قريش العذاب الذي أوعدوا به بقوله تعالى : والذين كذبوا بآياتنا يمسهم العذاب بما كانوا يفسقون) (۲) والمعنى أني لست بملك حتى يكون لي القوة والقدرة على إنزال العذاب بإذن الله كما كان لجبرئيل (عليه السلام)، أو يكون لي العلم بذلك بإخبار من الله بلا واسطة ومنها قوله تعالى : ( ما نهاكما ربكما عن هذه الشجرة إلا أن تكونا ملكين ) (۳). أي إلا كراهة أن تكونا ملكين. يعني أن الملكية بالمرتبة العليا، وفي الأكل من الشجرة ارتقاء إليها . والجواب أن ذلك تمويه من الشيطان وتخييل أن ما يشاهد في الملك من حسن الصورة، وعظم الخلق ، وكمال القوة يحصل بأكل الشجرة. ولوسلم فغاية التفضيل على آدم (عليه السلام) قبل النبوة. ( ومنها قوله تعالى : عَلَّمه شديد القوى ) ( ٤ ) . يعني جبرئيل (عليه السلام والمعلم أفضل من المتعلم . والجواب ان ذلك بطريق التبليغ، وإنما التعليم من الله تعالى. ومنها قوله تعالى: لن يستنكف المسيح أن يكون عبداً لله ولا الملائكة المقربون (٥) .
Eighth: That their deeds are more numerous, more enduring, and more upright, and their knowledge is more complete and abundant. And it was answered that what is accompanied by subduing the contrary and bearing hardships is more deserving of reward. Also by transmitted and rational proofs. As for transmitted proofs, among them is His saying, Exalted is He: 'And to Allah prostrates whatever is in the heavens and whatever is on the earth of creatures, and the angels, and they are not arrogant. They fear their Lord above them and do what they are commanded' (1). He distinguished them with humility and abandonment of arrogance in prostration. And in it is an indication that others are not like that, and that the causes of pride and self-magnification are present for them. And He described them with continuous fear and compliance with commands, among which is avoidance of prohibitions. And among them is His saying, Exalted is He: 'And those who are with Him are not arrogant toward His worship, nor do they become weary. They glorify [Him] night and day, never flagging' (2). He described them with proximity and honor with Him, and with humility and persistence in obedience and glorification. And among them is His saying, Exalted is He: 'Rather, they are honored servants. They do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command' (3)... until He said: 'And they are, from fear of Him, apprehensive.' And He singled them out with absolute honor, compliance, and fear, and these matters are the foundation of all good. The answer is that all of that only indicates their virtue (fadilah), not their superiority (afdaliyyah), especially over the prophets. And among them is His saying, Exalted is He: 'Say, I do not say to you that I possess the treasures of Allah, nor do I know the unseen, nor do I say to you that I am an angel' (1). For such speech is only appropriate if the angel is superior. And the answer is that he only said that when the Quraysh hastened him regarding the punishment that they were threatened with, by His saying, Exalted is He: 'And those who deny Our signs – the punishment will touch them because they used to defy' (2). The meaning is that I am not an angel so that I would have strength and power to send down punishment with Allah's permission, as was the case for Jibril (peace be upon him), or that I would have knowledge of that through a report from Allah without intermediary. And among them is His saying, Exalted is He: 'Your Lord did not forbid you this tree except that you become angels' (3). That is, except out of dislike that you become angels, meaning that angelhood is the supreme rank, and in eating from the tree there is ascension to it. The answer is that that is a sophistry from Satan and a suggestion that what is observed in the angel of beauty of form, greatness of creation, and perfection of power is obtained by eating the tree. And if it were granted, the utmost is superiority over Adam (peace be upon him) before prophethood. And among them is His saying, Exalted is He: 'Taught by one severe in power' (4), meaning Jibril (peace be upon him), and the teacher is better than the student. The answer is that that is by way of delivering, and teaching is only from Allah, Exalted is He. And among them is His saying, Exalted is He: 'The Messiah would never disdain to be a servant of Allah, nor would the angels brought near [to Him]' (5).
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a series of objections and answers regarding the superiority of angels over prophets. It begins with the eighth objection: that angels' deeds are more numerous, enduring, and upright, and their knowledge is more complete. The response states that deeds accompanied by overcoming opposition and bearing hardships are more deserving of reward—implying that prophets, who face greater trials, are more meritorious.

Then the author introduces transmitted and rational proofs for angelic superiority. The first transmitted proof is the verse from Surah an-Nahl (16:49-50), where angels prostrate humbly and obey constantly. The author interprets this as indicating their virtue but not superiority. Next is the verse from al-Anbiya (21:19-20) describing angels' continuous worship, again interpreted as virtue. Then the verse from al-Anbiya (21:26-28) calling them honored servants. The author concludes that all these verses only prove their virtue (fadilah), not absolute superiority (afdaliyyah), especially over prophets.

The author then addresses specific verses that might imply angelic superiority. The verse from al-An'am (6:50) where the Prophet (PBUH) says he does not claim to have treasures or be an angel is explained: it was said when the Quraysh demanded immediate punishment, meaning he lacked the angelic power to deliver it. Next, the verse from al-A'raf (7:20) where Iblees tempts Adam by saying the tree would make them angels is dismissed as a deception of Satan. Even if granted, it would only show angels' superiority over Adam before prophethood. The verse from an-Najm (53:5) that Jibril taught the Prophet is answered by noting that teaching is only from Allah, and Jibril is a messenger. Finally, the verse from an-Nisa (4:172) about the Messiah and angels not disdaining worship is likely presented as a proof of angelic piety, but the text cuts off before the response, implying a continuation.

The passage follows a systematic pattern: each proof for angelic superiority is presented and then refuted, either by reinterpreting the verse or by contextualizing its revelation.

Key Terms
فضيلة
أفضلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that because angels are described positively in many verses, they are superior to prophets.
Correction: The author clarifies that these verses indicate virtue, not absolute superiority, especially over prophets.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main response to the transmitted proofs from the Quran?
A) They are abrogated
B) They indicate angels' virtue, not superiority over prophets
C) They apply only to some angels
D) They prove prophets are superior

Key Takeaway
Quranic descriptions of angels' obedience demonstrate their virtue, not their superiority over prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone who seems more diligent in worship or more obedient than you, do you feel inferior or discouraged? How does the distinction between virtue and superiority change how you view yourself and others?
?
If the highest angels only possess virtue but not superiority over prophets, what does that imply about comparing yourself to those who have different roles or struggles?
?
Are there areas in your life where you mistake visible virtue for ultimate worth? How can you apply this lesson to avoid judging yourself or others unfairly?

Refutations of Specific Scriptural Proofs
Taftazani refutes four more transmitted proofs with specific answers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Taftazani refutes specific scriptural proofs for angelic superiority through contextual interpretation and by distinguishing roles.

Core Idea
Verses that seem to favor angels are either contextual or misinterpreted.

Taftazani continues by addressing more specific verses: the Prophet's denial of being an angel, the temptation of Adam, Jibril's teaching role, and the prostration verse. Each is given a precise response that neutralizes the claim of superiority. This lesson walks through these refutations.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses and arguments
Read each of the four remaining proofs: 6:50, 7:20, 53:5, and 4:172, along with the responses.
2
Analyze the contextual explanation for 6:50
Understand that the Prophet's statement was in response to Quraysh's demand for immediate punishment, not a claim of inferiority.
3
See the deception in 7:20
Recognize that the suggestion that eating the tree makes one an angel is a deception from Satan.
4
Understand the teaching role in 53:5
Note that Jibril is a deliverer, and the true teacher is Allah.

Answering the Objection from Quran 6:50
Author answers objection from Quran 6:50 about angelic superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author resolves the apparent implication of Quran 6:50 that angels are superior to prophets, showing the importance of context in interpreting theological objections.

Core Idea
Context reveals the Prophet's denial was about function, not rank.

The objection that prophets are inferior to angels often relies on a single verse where the Prophet denies being an angel. But careful reading shows that this verse was a specific response to the Quraysh's demand for immediate punishment. This lesson unpacks the objection and the author's precise answer, demonstrating how kalam handles scriptural challenges.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and the objection
Read the Arabic verse (Quran 6:50) and the objector's claim that such a statement only makes sense if angels are superior.
Notice the quotation marks in the Arabic: it begins with 'قل لا أقول لكم...'.
2
Understand the author's contextual answer
The author explains that the Prophet said this when the Quraysh were demanding immediate punishment. The Prophet meant he is not an angel who can inflict punishment instantly.
The answer hinges on the specific situation, not a general comparison.
3
Reflect on the principle: function vs. rank
Consider how distinguishing between function and rank resolves the objection. The Prophet lacked the angelic function of direct punishment, but that does not imply inferiority in rank.
This principle is key in kalam for handling similar objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قل لا أقول لكم عندي خزائن الله ولا أعلم الغيب ولا أقول إني ملك (١) فإن مثل هذا الكلام إنما يحسن إذا كان الملك أفضل والجواب أنه إنما قال حين استعجله قريش العذاب الذي أوعدوا به بقوله تعالى : والذين كذبوا بآياتنا يمسهم العذاب بما كانوا يفسقون) (٢) والمعنى أني لست بملك حتى يكون لي القوة والقدرة على إنزال العذاب بإذن الله كما كان لجبرئيل (عليه السلام)، أو يكون لي العلم بذلك بإخبار من الله بلا واسطة
Say: 'I do not say to you that I possess the treasures of Allah, nor do I know the unseen, nor do I say to you that I am an angel' (1). Indeed, such speech is only appropriate if the angel is superior. The answer is that he said it when the Quraysh hastened him with the punishment they were threatened with by His statement: 'And those who deny Our signs, the punishment will touch them because they used to transgress' (2). The meaning is that I am not an angel such that I have the power and ability to inflict punishment by Allah's permission as Jibril (peace be upon him) had, or that I have knowledge of that by direct revelation from Allah without intermediary.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objector argues that the Prophet's statement in the Quran (6:50) — where he denies possessing treasures, knowledge of the unseen, and being an angel — implies that angels are superior, because such a disclaimer would only be meaningful if the angelic state is higher. The author answers that the Prophet said this in a specific context: when the Quraysh demanded immediate punishment as threatened. The Prophet meant that he is not an angel with the power to bring down punishment instantly; rather, that power belongs to Jibril. Thus, the verse does not indicate superiority but merely a difference in function.

Key Terms
فضل
أفضلية
ملك
جبرئيل
خزائن الله
غيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse implies prophets are inferior to angels.
Correction: The verse was said when Quraysh demanded immediate punishment; the Prophet meant he is not an angel who can bring punishment, not that he is lower in rank.

Checkpoint
What is the author's answer to the objection that the Prophet's denial of being an angel implies angelic superiority?
A) The Prophet was being humble.
B) The Prophet said it when the Quraysh demanded immediate punishment, so he meant he is not an angel with power to inflict it.
C) The Prophet was comparing himself to the devils.
D) The verse was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The objection from Quran 6:50 is resolved by understanding its specific context: the Prophet denied being an angel because he lacked the angelic power to bring immediate punishment, not because angels are inherently superior.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does knowing the context—that he was answering a demand for immediate punishment—change your understanding of his authority and your trust in his prophethood? What might you risk by taking verses out of context in your own life?
?
The Quraysh demanded that God act on their timeline. Do you ever find yourself demanding that God answer your prayers or punish your enemies according to your schedule? What does this lesson teach you about trusting God's wisdom in delaying or withholding what you ask for?
?
If a single verse can be so misunderstood without its context, what other verses might you be misreading? What is your responsibility—right now—to seek deeper understanding before forming beliefs about Allah and His Prophet?

Answer to the objection from the tree verse
Author refutes the tree verse objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the verse 'except that you become angels' does not prove angelic superiority over prophets, and how the author exposes it as Satanic deception.

Core Idea
The tree verse is a Satanic illusion, not evidence of angelic superiority.

Some have argued that the Quranic story of Adam and the forbidden tree shows that angels are superior to prophets, because the devil tempted Adam to eat in order to become an angel. In this passage, the author refutes this claim by showing that the devil's words were a deception, and that at most they suggest a superiority over Adam before prophethood—not over prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how the author presents the objection first, then his answer.
The objection is based on a specific interpretation of Quran 7:20.
2
Identify the objector's claim
The objector says that the verse implies that becoming an angel is a higher rank, so the tree was forbidden to prevent Adam and Eve from reaching that rank.
3
Understand the author's response
The author gives two responses: 1) It is a deception from Satan, making them imagine physical angelic qualities. 2) Even if conceded, it only shows preference over Adam before prophethood, not over prophets.
This refutes the idea that angels are superior to all humans.
4
Connect to the broader topic
Consider how this fits into the larger discussion of prophethood and the status of angels. The passage defends the superiority of prophets.

Commentary
This passage addresses another objection from the Quran (7:20). The objector interprets the verse 'Your Lord did not forbid you this tree except that you become angels' as implying that becoming an angel is a higher state, and that eating from the tree would lead to that. The author answers that this is a deception from Satan, who made them imagine that the physical qualities of angels could be attained by eating. Even if one concedes that eating could lead to such qualities, it would only indicate preference over Adam before he became a prophet, not absolute superiority over prophets.

Jibril's Teaching: Transmission, Not Superiority
Author refutes that Jibril's teaching implies his superiority over the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the angel Jibril's act of teaching the Prophet does not imply his superiority over the Prophet, as the true teacher is Allah.

Core Idea
The angel is a messenger; the true teacher is Allah.

This passage addresses a common objection based on Quran 53:5. If Jibril taught the Prophet, does that make Jibril superior? The author provides a precise refutation by distinguishing between transmission and actual teaching. Let's read the passage and its explanation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the structure: an objection followed by an answer.
2
Identify the objection
The objection uses the verse to argue that the teacher (Jibril) is superior to the learner (the Prophet). Underline the phrase 'والمعلم أفضل من المتعلم'.
This is the core of the objection.
3
Understand the answer
The author responds by saying that Jibril's role is only transmission (تبليغ), not actual teaching. The real teacher is Allah. Reflect on how this distinction refutes the objection.
The key is the word 'تبليغ'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها قوله تعالى : عَلَّمه شديد القوى ) ( ٤ ) . يعني جبرئيل (عليه السلام) والمعلم أفضل من المتعلم . والجواب ان ذلك بطريق التبليغ، وإنما التعليم من الله تعالى.
And among them is His statement: 'Taught him one of severe powers' (4). Meaning Jibril (peace be upon him). And the teacher is superior to the learner. The answer is that that is by way of transmission, and teaching is only from Allah Almighty.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage deals with the argument that because Jibril taught the Prophet, as mentioned in Quran 53:5, the teacher (Jibril) must be superior to the learner (Muhammad). The author answers that Jibril's role is only that of a messenger conveying revelation; the actual teaching originates from Allah. Thus, the verse does not imply Jibril's superiority over the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jibril is superior to the Prophet because he taught him.
Correction: Jibril's teaching is only transmission; the true teacher is Allah, so no superiority is established.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The act of conveying revelation does not confer superiority; the source of teaching is Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Answer to the Objection from the Verse about Angels Near to Allah
Author refutes the claim that 'المقربون' implies angelic superiority over prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the term 'المقربون' in Quran 4:172 does not imply the superiority of angels over prophets, but rather highlights their station as a context for not disdaining worship.

Core Idea
Being 'near to Allah' does not mean superior in virtue; it means less likely to disdain worship.

We often assume that the Quranic description 'المقربون' for angels indicates their superiority over prophets. This lesson shows that the verse actually addresses a specific refutation of Christian claims, and the term is used to emphasize that even high beings submit to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and the objection
Start with the Quranic verse (4:172) and understand why someone might think it implies angelic superiority. The objector focuses on the phrase 'المقربون' as a point of argument.
Note that the objection assumes that singling out angels indicates their higher status.
2
Analyze the author's example
The author provides a rhetorical example: 'the vizier nor the sultan will disdain this matter'. See how the structure works and what it implies about the intention of the comparison.
The example shows that mentioning a higher-ranking figure does not necessarily mean they are superior in all aspects.
3
Grasp the refutation
The author explains the actual context: the verse was revealed to refute Christian claims about Jesus' divinity and sonship, not to rank angels above prophets. The term 'المقربون' highlights that even beings without human limitations do not disdain worship.
The example from Surah Al-Baqarah 120 is also used to support this interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها قوله تعالى: لن يستنكف المسيح أن يكون عبداً لله ولا الملائكة المقربون (٥) . أي لا يترفع عيسى في العبودية، ولا من هو أرفع منه درجة، كقولك : لن يستنكف من هذا الأمر الوزير ولا السلطان. ولو عكست أحلت بشهادة علماء البيان والبصراء بأساليب الكلام وعليه قوله تعالى : ولن ترضى عنك اليهود ولا النصارى (١) . أي مع أنهم أقرب مودة لأصل الإسلام، ولهذا خص الملائكة بالمقربين منهم لكونهم أفضل . والجواب أن الكلام سبق لرد مقالة النصارى وغيرهم في المسيح وادعائهم فيه النبوة البنوة، بل الألوهية والترفع عن العبودية لكونه روح الله ، ولد بلا أب ولكونه يبرىء الأكمه والأبرص والمعنى لا يترفع عيسى عن العبودية (٢) ولا من هو فوقه في هذا المعنى، وهم الملائكة الذين لا أب لهم ولا أم ويقدرون على ما لا يقدر عليه عیسی (علیه السلام)، ولا دلالة على الأفضلية بمعنى كثرة الثواب وسائر الكمالات، ألا یری أن فيما ذكرت من المثال لم يقصد الزيادة والرفعة في الفضل والشرف والكمال، بل فيما هو مظنة الاستنكاف والرضا كالغلبة والاستكبار والاستعلاء في السلطان وقرب المودة في النصارى.
And among them is His statement: 'The Messiah will never disdain to be a servant of Allah, nor the angels who are near [to Allah]' (5). Meaning Jesus does not exalt himself in servitude, nor does anyone higher in degree than him, like your saying: 'The vizier nor the sultan will disdain this matter.' And if you reversed it, you would err, according to the testimony of scholars of rhetoric and experts in styles of speech. And based on it is His statement: 'And never will the Jews and Christians be pleased with you' (1). Meaning even though they are closer in affection to the origin of Islam, and for this reason he singled out angels as 'those near' among them because they are superior. The answer is that the speech was said to refute the claim of the Christians and others concerning the Messiah and their claim of prophecy, sonship, and even divinity and exaltation from servitude because he is the Spirit of Allah, born without a father, and because he heals the blind and leprous. And the meaning is that Jesus does not exalt himself from servitude, nor does anyone above him in this sense, and they are the angels who have no father or mother and are able to do what Jesus cannot. And there is no indication of superiority in the sense of abundance of reward and other perfections. Do you not see that in the example mentioned, the intent was not increase and elevation in virtue, honor, and perfection, but rather in what is presumed to involve disdain and satisfaction, like dominance, arrogance, and superiority in the sultan, and closeness in affection among the Christians.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage addresses the objection from Quran 4:172. The objector argues that since the verse mentions 'angels who are near' as not disdaining worship, and singles them out as 'المقربون', they must be superior. The author first explains that the verse is about disdaining servitude, not about ranking, and gives an example: if one says 'the vizier nor the sultan will disdain this', it does not mean the sultan is superior in all respects, but rather that they are less likely to disdain. Similarly, the angels are mentioned because they are more likely to be thought of as disdaining worship due to their high rank, not because they are superior in virtue. The answer further clarifies that the verse was revealed in refutation of Christian claims about Jesus' divinity, showing that Jesus is a servant of Allah like the angels, and no superiority is indicated.

Key Terms

عبودية
مقربون
مسيح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Angels are superior to prophets because they are called 'المقربون' in the verse.
Correction: The term 'المقربون' is used to indicate that even high-ranking beings do not disdain worship, not to establish overall superiority.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why are angels specifically called 'المقربون' in the verse 'لن يستنكف المسيح...'?
A) Because they are superior to all prophets.
B) Because they are more likely to be thought of as disdaining worship due to their high station.
C) Because they are the closest creation to Allah.
D) Because they are mentioned alongside Jesus.

Key Takeaway
The verse does not indicate angelic superiority; it refutes Christian claims by showing that even high beings like angels submit to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever interpreted a Quranic verse based on your initial assumption, only to realize later that context changed the meaning? How does this lesson challenge you to pause before forming conclusions about Allah's words? Will you commit to studying the Quran with more humility and attention to rhetorical details?
?
The author uses an everyday example to correct a misunderstanding. Think of a belief you hold about Islam that you've never questioned deeply. What if your belief is based on a similar oversight of rhetorical context? Are you willing to re-examine it, even if it feels uncomfortable?
?
The lesson shows that even the highest beings—angels—do not disdain worship. Reflect on your own worship: are there moments when you feel a sense of superiority or reluctance? How can the example of the angels, who never disdain despite their high rank, motivate you to approach worship with more sincerity and humility? What will you change starting today?

Answering the Objection from the Verse about Jews and Christians
First objection from a Quranic verse and its answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the claim that mentioning angels as 'close ones' in a verse implies their superiority over prophets.

Core Idea
The verse's context refutes Christian claims, not superiority.

The first objection arises from a specific Quranic verse that seems to elevate angels. The author carefully explains the context of the verse and shows that its purpose is not to establish superiority in rank or reward. Instead, it addresses the occasion of disdain and closeness to Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and its basis
Read the passage from 'أي لا يترفع عيسى' to the end of the first answer. Notice how the objection is derived from the verse and the interpretation that angels are 'the close ones'.
The objection uses the verse 'ولن ترضى عنك اليهود ولا النصارى'.
2
Identify the author's response
The author explains that the verse was revealed to refute Christian beliefs about Jesus, not to compare angels and prophets. The mention of angels as 'close ones' is about their closeness to Islam, not superiority.
The answer emphasizes context over literal precedence.
3
Analyze the example provided
The author gives an example of saying 'the minister nor the sultan will not disdain this matter' to show that the wording does not imply superiority in all aspects.
The example illustrates that the focus is on the occasion of disdain, not on overall excellence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي لا يترفع عيسى في العبودية، ولا من هو أرفع منه درجة، كقولك : لن يستنكف من هذا الأمر الوزير ولا السلطان. ولو عكست أحلت بشهادة علماء البيان والبصراء بأساليب الكلام وعليه قوله تعالى : ولن ترضى عنك اليهود ولا النصارى . أي مع أنهم أقرب مودة لأصل الإسلام، ولهذا خص الملائكة بالمقربين منهم لكونهم أفضل . والجواب أن الكلام سبق لرد مقالة النصارى وغيرهم في المسيح وادعائهم فيه النبوة البنوة، بل الألوهية والترفع عن العبودية لكونه روح الله ، ولد بلا أب ولكونه يبرىء الأكمه والأبرص والمعنى لا يترفع عيسى عن العبودية ولا من هو فوقه في هذا المعنى، وهم الملائكة الذين لا أب لهم ولا أم ويقدرون على ما لا يقدر عليه عیسی (علیه السلام)، ولا دلالة على الأفضلية بمعنى كثرة الثواب وسائر الكمالات، ألا یری أن فيما ذكرت من المثال لم يقصد الزيادة والرفعة في الفضل والشرف والكمال، بل فيما هو مظنة الاستنكاف والرضا كالغلبة والاستكبار والاستعلاء في السلطان وقرب المودة في النصارى. ومنها اطراد تقديم ذكر الملائكة على ذكر الأنبياء والرسل، ولا يعقل له جهة سوى الأفضلية. والجواب أنه يجوز أن يكون بجهة تقدمهم في الوجود، أو في قوة الإيمان بهم والاهتمام به لأنهم أخفى، فالإيمان بهم أقوى، وبالتحريض عليه أحرى. وأما العقليات فمنها أن الملائكة روحانيات مجردة في ذواتها متعلقة بالهياكل العلوية، مبرأة عن ظلمة المادة، وعن الشهوة والغضب اللذين هما مبدأ الشرور والقبائح متصفة بالكمالات العلمية والعملية بالعقل من غير شوائب الجهل والنقص والخروج من القوة إلى الفعل على التدريج، ومن احتمال الغلط قوية على الأفعال العجيبة وإحداث السحب والزلازل، وأمثال ذلك، مطلعة على أسرار الغيب سابقة إلى أنواع الخير، ولا كذلك حال البشر. والجواب أن مبنی ذلك على قواعد الفلسفة دون الملة . ومنها أن أعمالهم المستوجبة للمثوبات أكثر لطول زمانهم، وأدوم لعدم تخلل الشواغل، وأقوم لسلامتها عن مخالطة المعاصي المنقصة للثواب، وعلومهم أكمل وأكثر لكونهم نورانيين روحانيين، يشاهدون اللوح المحفوظ المنتقش بالكائنات، وأسرار المغيبات. والجواب أن هذا لا يمنع كون أعمال الأنبياء وعلومهم أفضل وأكثر ثواباً لجهات أخر، كقهر المضاد والمنافي، وتحمل المتاعب والمشاق، ونحو ذلك على ما مر.
That is, Jesus does not disdain servitude, nor does anyone higher in degree than him, as you say: 'The minister nor the sultan will not disdain this matter.' And if you reversed, you would make a mistake by the testimony of scholars of eloquence and those with insight into styles of speech. And upon it is His saying, the Most High: 'And never will the Jews nor the Christians be pleased with you.' That is, while they are closer in affection to the origin of Islam, and for this reason He specifically mentioned the angels among them as the close ones because they are superior. The answer: The speech was already to refute the statement of the Christians and others concerning the Messiah and their claim in him of prophethood, sonship, rather divinity, and disdain of servitude because he is the Spirit of God, born without a father, and because he cures the blind and the leprous. And the meaning is: Jesus does not disdain servitude, nor anyone above him in this meaning, and they are the angels who have no father or mother and are able to do what Jesus (peace be upon him) cannot. And there is no indication of superiority in the sense of abundance of reward and other perfections. Do you not see that in what you mentioned of the example, the increase and exaltation in virtue, honor, and perfection was not intended, but rather what is the occasion for disdain and satisfaction like dominance, arrogance, and haughtiness in the sultan, and closeness of affection in the Christians. And among them (the objections) is the consistent precedence of mentioning angels over mentioning prophets and messengers, and no reason for it can be conceived other than superiority. The answer: It is possible that it is due to their precedence in existence, or in the strength of faith in them and concern for them because they are more hidden, so faith in them is stronger, and incitement to it is more appropriate. As for rational (objections), among them is that the angels are spiritual entities abstract in their essences, attached to the celestial structures, free from the darkness of matter, and from lust and anger which are the origin of evils and ugly deeds, characterized by intellectual and practical perfections by reason without any admixture of ignorance and deficiency and gradual transition from potentiality to actuality, and from the possibility of error, powerful over wondrous acts and causing clouds and earthquakes and the like, informed of the secrets of the unseen, preceding to all kinds of good, and such is not the case of humans. The answer: That is based on the principles of philosophy, not on the (divine) law. And among them (the objections) is that their works that necessitate rewards are more due to the length of their time, and more enduring due to the absence of interruptions, and more upright due to their safety from mixing with sins that diminish reward, and their knowledge is more complete and more abundant because they are luminous spiritual beings, observing the Preserved Tablet inscribed with all beings and the secrets of the unseen. The answer: This does not prevent the works and knowledge of the prophets from being better and more rewarding for other aspects, such as overcoming opposition and obstacles, bearing hardships and difficulties, and the like, as mentioned before.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a series of three objections and answers defending the superiority of prophets over angels. The first objection arises from the verse 'And never will the Jews nor the Christians be pleased with you' and the mention of angels as 'the close ones'. The author explains that the context is refuting Christian claims about Jesus, and the mention of angels does not indicate superiority in reward or perfection, but rather in the occasion of disdain. The second objection is the consistent pattern of mentioning angels before prophets in the Quran. The answer is that this may be due to their precedence in existence or the strength of faith in them since they are hidden. The third objection presents rational arguments: angels are spiritual, free from matter, lust, and anger, powerful, and know the unseen. The author responds that these are philosophical principles, not religious ones. A further rational argument is that angels' good deeds and knowledge are more abundant and enduring. The answer is that prophets have other aspects like overcoming opposition and bearing hardships that make their deeds superior.

Key Terms
العبودية
الملائكة
الأنبياء
الأفضلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'ولن ترضى عنك اليهود ولا النصارى' proves angels are superior to prophets.
Correction: The verse addresses Christian claims about Jesus, not a comparison between angels and prophets; the mention of angels is to highlight that even they do not disdain servitude.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the verse was revealed?
A) To prove angels are better than prophets.
B) To refute Christian claims about Jesus.
C) To show that Jews and Christians will never be pleased.
D) To establish the superiority of the 'close ones'.

Key Takeaway
The verse about Jews and Christians does not imply angelic superiority; it is about refuting Christian claims regarding Jesus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a Quranic verse that seems to confirm a belief you already hold, do you pause to investigate its context and original purpose, as the author did here? How can you train yourself to look deeper before drawing conclusions?
?
The author shows that the verse was a direct response to specific false claims about Jesus. Are there any Islamic teachings you have accepted without checking the original context? What is one teaching you will revisit this week to ensure your understanding is accurate?
?
The example of the minister and sultan illustrates that wording can highlight a particular quality without implying general superiority. In your own life, where might you be misinterpreting others' words by focusing on the wrong aspect? Commit to one conversation where you will listen for the intended meaning rather than assuming superiority or inferiority.

Answering the Objection from Precedence of Mention
Second objection from consistent precedence in mention and its answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the consistent precedence of angels over prophets in Quranic mention does not necessarily indicate their superiority.

Core Idea
Precedence in mention can be due to other reasons, not superiority.

The second objection points to the consistent pattern in the Quran where angels are mentioned before prophets. The author offers two plausible alternative reasons for this order: precedence in existence and the strength of faith required for belief in the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the sentence starting with 'ومنها اطراد تقديم ذكر الملائكة على ذكر الأنبياء والرسل' and understand the claim that the only conceivable reason for this consistent precedence is superiority.
The objection assumes that if there were no superiority, the order would not be consistently maintained.
2
Study the answer
The author provides two possibilities: precedence in existence (angels were created before prophets) or strength of faith (believing in angels, who are hidden, requires stronger faith).
Note that these are legitimate reasons that have nothing to do with superiority.
3
Reflect on the logic
Consider why the author does not say 'maybe it is just a stylistic choice' – he gives reasons grounded in Islamic theology and psychology.
The answer shows that alternative explanations are sufficient to undermine the objection.

أي لا يترفع عيسى في العبودية، ولا من هو أرفع منه درجة، كقولك : لن يستنكف من هذا الأمر الوزير ولا السلطان. ولو عكست أحلت بشهادة علماء البيان والبصراء بأساليب الكلام وعليه قوله تعالى : ولن ترضى عنك اليهود ولا النصارى . أي مع أنهم أقرب مودة لأصل الإسلام، ولهذا خص الملائكة بالمقربين منهم لكونهم أفضل . والجواب أن الكلام سبق لرد مقالة النصارى وغيرهم في المسيح وادعائهم فيه النبوة البنوة، بل الألوهية والترفع عن العبودية لكونه روح الله ، ولد بلا أب ولكونه يبرىء الأكمه والأبرص والمعنى لا يترفع عيسى عن العبودية ولا من هو فوقه في هذا المعنى، وهم الملائكة الذين لا أب لهم ولا أم ويقدرون على ما لا يقدر عليه عیسی (علیه السلام)، ولا دلالة على الأفضلية بمعنى كثرة الثواب وسائر الكمالات، ألا یری أن فيما ذكرت من المثال لم يقصد الزيادة والرفعة في الفضل والشرف والكمال، بل فيما هو مظنة الاستنكاف والرضا كالغلبة والاستكبار والاستعلاء في السلطان وقرب المودة في النصارى. ومنها اطراد تقديم ذكر الملائكة على ذكر الأنبياء والرسل، ولا يعقل له جهة سوى الأفضلية. والجواب أنه يجوز أن يكون بجهة تقدمهم في الوجود، أو في قوة الإيمان بهم والاهتمام به لأنهم أخفى، فالإيمان بهم أقوى، وبالتحريض عليه أحرى. وأما العقليات فمنها أن الملائكة روحانيات مجردة في ذواتها متعلقة بالهياكل العلوية، مبرأة عن ظلمة المادة، وعن الشهوة والغضب اللذين هما مبدأ الشرور والقبائح متصفة بالكمالات العلمية والعملية بالعقل من غير شوائب الجهل والنقص والخروج من القوة إلى الفعل على التدريج، ومن احتمال الغلط قوية على الأفعال العجيبة وإحداث السحب والزلازل، وأمثال ذلك، مطلعة على أسرار الغيب سابقة إلى أنواع الخير، ولا كذلك حال البشر. والجواب أن مبنی ذلك على قواعد الفلسفة دون الملة . ومنها أن أعمالهم المستوجبة للمثوبات أكثر لطول زمانهم، وأدوم لعدم تخلل الشواغل، وأقوم لسلامتها عن مخالطة المعاصي المنقصة للثواب، وعلومهم أكمل وأكثر لكونهم نورانيين روحانيين، يشاهدون اللوح المحفوظ المنتقش بالكائنات، وأسرار المغيبات. والجواب أن هذا لا يمنع كون أعمال الأنبياء وعلومهم أفضل وأكثر ثواباً لجهات أخر، كقهر المضاد والمنافي، وتحمل المتاعب والمشاق، ونحو ذلك على ما مر.
That is, Jesus does not disdain servitude, nor does anyone higher in degree than him, as you say: 'The minister nor the sultan will not disdain this matter.' And if you reversed, you would make a mistake by the testimony of scholars of eloquence and those with insight into styles of speech. And upon it is His saying, the Most High: 'And never will the Jews nor the Christians be pleased with you.' That is, while they are closer in affection to the origin of Islam, and for this reason He specifically mentioned the angels among them as the close ones because they are superior. The answer: The speech was already to refute the statement of the Christians and others concerning the Messiah and their claim in him of prophethood, sonship, rather divinity, and disdain of servitude because he is the Spirit of God, born without a father, and because he cures the blind and the leprous. And the meaning is: Jesus does not disdain servitude, nor anyone above him in this meaning, and they are the angels who have no father or mother and are able to do what Jesus (peace be upon him) cannot. And there is no indication of superiority in the sense of abundance of reward and other perfections. Do you not see that in what you mentioned of the example, the increase and exaltation in virtue, honor, and perfection was not intended, but rather what is the occasion for disdain and satisfaction like dominance, arrogance, and haughtiness in the sultan, and closeness of affection in the Christians. And among them (the objections) is the consistent precedence of mentioning angels over mentioning prophets and messengers, and no reason for it can be conceived other than superiority. The answer: It is possible that it is due to their precedence in existence, or in the strength of faith in them and concern for them because they are more hidden, so faith in them is stronger, and incitement to it is more appropriate. As for rational (objections), among them is that the angels are spiritual entities abstract in their essences, attached to the celestial structures, free from the darkness of matter, and from lust and anger which are the origin of evils and ugly deeds, characterized by intellectual and practical perfections by reason without any admixture of ignorance and deficiency and gradual transition from potentiality to actuality, and from the possibility of error, powerful over wondrous acts and causing clouds and earthquakes and the like, informed of the secrets of the unseen, preceding to all kinds of good, and such is not the case of humans. The answer: That is based on the principles of philosophy, not on the (divine) law. And among them (the objections) is that their works that necessitate rewards are more due to the length of their time, and more enduring due to the absence of interruptions, and more upright due to their safety from mixing with sins that diminish reward, and their knowledge is more complete and more abundant because they are luminous spiritual beings, observing the Preserved Tablet inscribed with all beings and the secrets of the unseen. The answer: This does not prevent the works and knowledge of the prophets from being better and more rewarding for other aspects, such as overcoming opposition and obstacles, bearing hardships and difficulties, and the like, as mentioned before.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a series of three objections and answers defending the superiority of prophets over angels. The first objection arises from the verse 'And never will the Jews nor the Christians be pleased with you' and the mention of angels as 'the close ones'. The author explains that the context is refuting Christian claims about Jesus, and the mention of angels does not indicate superiority in reward or perfection, but rather in the occasion of disdain. The second objection is the consistent pattern of mentioning angels before prophets in the Quran. The answer is that this may be due to their precedence in existence or the strength of faith in them since they are hidden. The third objection presents rational arguments: angels are spiritual, free from matter, lust, and anger, powerful, and know the unseen. The author responds that these are philosophical principles, not religious ones. A further rational argument is that angels' good deeds and knowledge are more abundant and enduring. The answer is that prophets have other aspects like overcoming opposition and bearing hardships that make their deeds superior.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The consistent precedence of angels in Quranic mention proves they are superior.
Correction: Other valid reasons exist, such as precedence in creation or the strength of faith required to believe in them.

Checkpoint
What two reasons does the author give for the precedence of angels in mention?
A) They are stronger and more powerful.
B) They were created first and require stronger faith.
C) They have more knowledge and longer lives.
D) They are free from sin and closer to Allah.

Key Takeaway
Precedence in mention does not prove superiority; other explanations like order of creation or degree of faith are plausible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran and notice that angels are mentioned before prophets, do you ever feel a pull toward assuming their superiority? How often do you stop to consider that the order might be teaching you something about your own faith—that belief in the unseen requires a stronger, more active trust? What would it take for you to really grapple with that hiddenness instead of simply ranking them?
?
The objector assumed only one reason explains the Quranic pattern. In your own life, how often do you jump to a single conclusion about God's wisdom in a certain matter, forgetting that He may have multiple, layered purposes that you haven't considered? Can you name one area where you've assumed you know God's reason, and commit to asking Him to open your eyes to other possibilities?
?
The author says faith in angels is stronger because they are hidden. Think about your own faith: is your belief in angels something active and constant, or is it more of a passive acceptance? How would your daily life change if you truly lived with the awareness that unseen angels are witnessing your actions and protecting you? What one habit could you start today to increase your consciousness of them?
